Phrases That Establish Kafalah
Ruling on valid phrases for kafalah with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which verbal phrases create a valid kafalah bi al-nafs in the Hanafi school and identify the exception that does not.

Core Idea
Kafalah is established by explicit undertaking phrases, not by mere recognition.

This lesson covers the specific verbal formulas that immediately create a kafalah contract in Hanafi law. The text lists several phrases, explains their rationale, and provides Prophetic proof. Understanding which expressions are valid and which are not is essential for correctly drafting or interpreting kafalah agreements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act in question is kafalah bi al-nafs (guarantee of a person's presence). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) when using any of the listed phrases.
2
List the Valid Phrases
From the text: 'ضمنته', 'هو على', 'هو إلى', 'أنا زعيم به', 'أنا قبيل'. Each explicitly or customarily indicates undertaking responsibility.
Note that 'هو إلى' is supported by a hadith where the Prophet used 'إلى' meaning 'على'.
3
Understand the Rationale
Each phrase is either an explicit statement of the contract's effect (e.g., 'ضمنته') or a formula of undertaking ('هو على'), or a customary synonym ('زعيم', 'قبيل').
The contract is established by explicit expression of its purpose, similar to sale by 'تمليك'.
4
Identify the Exception
The phrase 'أنا ضامن لمعرفته' (I guarantee recognition) does not create kafalah because it undertakes only identification, not the demand for the person.
Kafalah requires undertaking the demand for the person (التزام المطالبة).
5
Note the Proof from Hadith
The Prophet's hadith: 'من ترك مالا فلورثته ومن ترك كلا أو ضياعا فإلى' uses 'إلى' to mean 'upon', showing that 'هو إلى' can validly create responsibility.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for this ruling.

Source Text

تشریح امام ابوالحسن قدوری نے فرمایا کہ لفظ ضمنته ( میں فلاں کے نفس کا ضامن ہو گیا) کہنے سے بھی کفالہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے کیونکہ لفظ ضمان ادا کرنے سے عقد کفالہ کے موجب کی صراحت ہو گئی ہے اور عقد چونکہ موجب کی تصریح کرنے سے منعقد ہو جاتا ہے اسلئے لفظ ضمان سے کفالہ منعقد ہو جائے گا جیسے عقد بیع لفظ تملیک سے منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تملیک عقد بیع کا موجب ہے اور اگر کہاھو علی یعنی میں نے اپنے اوپر لازم کیا کہ جب اس کی حاضری مطلوب ہوگی تو میں اس کو حاضر کروں گا۔ اس سے بھی کفالہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ على التزام کا صیغہ ہے اور کفالہ میں بھی چونکہ مطالبہ کا التزام ہوتا ہے اسلئے لفظ علی سے کفالہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر کہا ھو الی یعنی وہ میری طرف ہے تو اس سے بھی کفالہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ الی اس مقام میں علی کے معنی میں ہے اور لفظ علمی سے کفالہ چونکہ منعقد ہو جاتا ہے۔ اسلئے لفظ الی سے بھی منعقد ہو جائے گا اور لفظ الی کا علی کے معنی میں ہونا حدیث سے بھی ثابت ہے کیونکہ رسول اکرم من ترک مالا فلورثته و من ترک کلا او عیالا فالتی یعنی جس نے مال چھوڑا
کا ارشاد ہے وہ تو اس کے وارثوں کے واسطے ہے۔ اور جس نے یتیم اولا دیا پرورش کے محتاج قرابتدار چھوڑے تو ان کی ذمہ داری مجھ پر ہے یعنی میں ان کا کفیل ہوں ۔ ملاحظہ فرمایئے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے الی کو علی کے معنی میں استعمال کیا ہے اور اگر انسٹا زعیم یا انا قبیل کہا تب بھی کفالہ منعقد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ زعامت بھی کفالت کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے۔ جیسا کہ حدیث الزعيم غارم میں وارد ہوا ہے اور قبیل کے معنی بھی کفیل کے آتے ہیں ۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ چک اور دستاویز کو قبالہ کہا جاتا ہے کیونکہ انسان جو کچھ دستاویز میں لکھتا ہے وہ سب اپنے اوپر لازم کرتا ہے اور اپنے اوپر لازم کرنے والے ہی کو فیل کہا جاتا ہے اسلئے انا قبیل انا کفیل کے معنی میں ہوگا۔ ہاں اگر کسی نے مکفول بنفسہ کے بارے میں کہا کہ میں اس کو شناخت کرنے کا ضامن ہوں تو اس سے کفالہ منعقد نہ ہوگا کیونکہ اس صورت میں کفیل نے شناخت کرنے کا التزام کیا ہے۔ مطالبہ کا التزام نہیں کیا ہے حالانکہ کفالہ التزام مطالبہ کا نام ہے۔ مکفول بنفسہ کو شناخت کرنے کے التزام کا نام کفالہ نہیں ۔
Kafalah is also established by the word 'ضمنته' (I guarantee him). Similarly, if he said 'ضمنته' (I guarantee him) because it is explicit about its effect, or he said 'هو على' (he is upon me) because it is a form of undertaking, or he said 'هو إلى' (he is towards me) because in this context it has the meaning of 'على'. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs; and whoever leaves a burden (children/dependents) [without support], then they are towards me.' Similarly, if he said 'أنا زعيم به' (I am a guarantor for him) or 'قبيل' because 'زعامة' is kafalah, and we have narrated a hadith about it, and 'قبيل' is the kafil. For this reason, the document (صك) is called 'قبالة'. Contrary to if he said 'أنا ضامن لمعرفته' (I guarantee his recognition) because it is an undertaking of recognition, not of demand.
Translation: Similarly, if he said 'I am his guarantor,' because this is explicit about the effect of kafalah; or he said 'he is upon me,' because it is a formula of undertaking; or he said 'he is towards me,' because it has the meaning of 'upon' in this context. The Prophet said: 'Whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs; and whoever leaves a burden (orphans/dependents) [without support], they are towards me.' Similarly, if he said 'I am a za'eem (guarantor) of his guarantee' or 'qabeel,' because 'zamamah' is kafalah, and we have narrated a hadith about it, and 'qabeel' is the kafil. For this reason, the document is called 'qabalah'. Contrary to if someone said 'I am a guarantor of his recognition,' because he has undertaken recognition, not the demand.
Explanation: Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: The word 'ضمنته' (I became the guarantor of his person) also establishes kafalah because the word 'ضمان' explicitly states the effect of the kafalah contract, and a contract is established by explicitly stating its effect. Therefore, kafalah is established by the word 'ضمان', just as a sale contract is established by the word 'تمليك' because 'تمليك' is the effect of a sale contract. And if he said 'هو على' i.e., 'I have taken upon myself that when his presence is demanded, I will bring him,' then kafalah is also established because the word 'على' is a formula of undertaking, and since kafalah involves undertaking the demand, kafalah is established by 'على'. And if he said 'هو إلى' i.e., 'he is towards me,' then kafalah is also established because the word 'إلى' in this context has the meaning of 'على', and since kafalah is established by 'على', it is also established by 'إلى'. And that 'إلى' has the meaning of 'على' is also proven by hadith, because the Prophet said: 'Whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs; and whoever leaves a burden (orphans) [without support], then 'فإلى' (they are towards me)'. Note that the Prophet used 'إلى' in the meaning of 'على'. And if he said 'أنا زعيم' or 'أنا قبيل', then also kafalah is established. Because 'زعامة' is used in the meaning of kafalah, as mentioned in the hadith 'الزعيم غارم', and 'قبيل' means kafil. For this reason, a document (صك) is called 'قبالة' because whatever a person writes in a document, he takes it upon himself, and the one who takes something upon himself is called 'قبيل'. So 'أنا قبيل' means 'I am a kafil'. However, if someone said about the makful bihi (the person guaranteed) 'I am the guarantor of recognizing him,' then kafalah is not established because in this case the kafil undertook recognition, not the demand. Kafalah is the undertaking of the demand. Undertaking to recognize the makful bihi is not called kafalah.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof on the phrases that establish kafalah. The passage lists several phrases: 'ضمنته' (I guarantee him) - explicit; 'هو على' (he is upon me) - a form of undertaking; 'هو إلى' (he is towards me) - meaning the same as 'على' in this context, supported by a hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) where he used 'إلى' to mean responsibility. Also 'أنا زعيم' (I am a guarantor) and 'أنا قبيل' (I am a kafil) are valid; 'زعامة' and 'قبيل' are synonymous with kafalah. The exception is 'ضامن لمعرفته' (guarantor of recognition) which only guarantees identification, not the demand for presence, so it does not constitute kafalah. The commentator explains the reasoning: each phrase explicitly or customarily denotes undertaking personal responsibility.

Key Terms
ضمنته (dhamintuhu): I guarantee him; a verbal expression that explicitly creates the kafalah contract.
زعيم (za'eem): Guarantor, one who takes responsibility for another's appearance or debt.
قبيل (qabeel): Kafil; one who accepts responsibility and is the same as 'كفيل'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Kafalah al-nafs is established by explicit or customary phrases of undertaking, but not by a mere guarantee of recognition.

Kafalah — Surety

Conditioning Time in Kafalah bi al-Nafs
Ruling on time condition in personal guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a time-conditioned kafalah bi al-nafs and identify the conditions for the kafil's obligation and the judicial process for non-compliance.

Core Idea
A time condition makes the kafil's obligation due only on demand at that time, with imprisonment only after a fair process.

This passage from the Hanafi tradition explains the effect of conditioning a specific time for the delivery of the guaranteed person (makful bihi) in a personal guarantee (kafalah bi al-nafs). The ruling clarifies when the kafil must act and what consequences follow non-compliance, ensuring the kafil is not punished without establishing willful refusal or after allowing reasonable efforts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kafalah bi al-nafs with an explicit condition specifying a time for delivery. The ruling is that the kafil must bring the makful bihi only when the claimant (makful lahu) demands him at that specific time.
This is not an unconditional obligation; demand is a trigger.
2
List the conditions for the kafil's obligation
The obligation to produce is conditional on: (a) a valid kafalah contract, (b) an explicit time condition, and (c) a demand by the makful lahu at that specified time. Without demand, the kafil is not required to act.
The condition of time is set by the parties; it must be explicit.
3
Trace the consequences of non-compliance
If the kafil fails to produce after a valid demand, the judge does not imprison immediately. First, the judge considers whether the kafil knew the claim. If the makful bihi is absent, the judge grants a travel period (duration of going and coming). Only after that period passes without production does the judge imprison the kafil, confirming refusal.
The process protects the kafil from hasty punishment.
4
Explain the procedural safeguards
The judge does not imprison on the first failure because the kafil might not know the reason for the suit. If the guaranteed person is absent, the kafil gets a reasonable time to locate and bring him. These safeguards ensure fairness.
Imprisonment is a last resort after due process.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The ruling as stated is the operative (mufta bihi) position: the kafil must produce the makful bihi when demanded at the specified time, and the judge follows the described graduated enforcement.
This is the relied-upon ruling in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال : فإن شرط في الكفالة بالنفس تسليم المكفول به فى وقت بعينه لزمه احضاره اذا طالبه فی ذلک الوقت وفاء بما التزمه فان احضره والاحبسه الحاكم لا متناعه عن ايفاء حق مستحق عليه ولكن لا يحبسه اول مرة فلطه مادرى لما ذا يداعى ولو غاب المكفول بنفسه امهله الحاكم مدة ذهابه ومجيئه فان مضت ولم يحضره يحبسه لتحقق امتناعه عن ايفاء الحق
ترجمہ پھر اگر کفالہ بالنفس میں مکفول بہ کو وقت معین میں سپرد کرنے کی شرط کی ہو تو کفیل پر مکفول کو حاضر کرنا لازم ہوگا ۔ بشرطیکہ مکفول لۂ اس وقت میں کفیل سے مطالبہ کرے تا کہ جو اس نے التزام کیا ہے وہ پورا کرے۔ پس اگر کفیل نے اس کو حاضر کر دیا ( تو فبہا ) ور نہ حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا کیونکہ وہ ایسا حق ادا کرنے سے رک گیا ہے۔ جو اس پر واجب ہے لیکن حاکم اس کو پہلی ہی مرتبہ قید نہ کرے گا۔ کیونکہ شاید اس کو معلوم نہ ہو کہ کیوں بلایا گیا ہے اور اگر مکفول بنفسہ غائب ہو گیا تو حاکم اس کو آمد و رفت کی مدت تک مہلت دے گا۔ پس اگر مدت گذرگئی اور کفیل اس کو حاضر نہ کر سکا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا کیونکہ حق ادا کرنے سے اس کار کنا متحقق ہو گیا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کفالہ بالنفس میں ایک معینہ وقت میں مکفول بنفسہ کو سپر د کرنے کی شرط کی گئی تو کفیل پر اس وقت معینہ میں مکفول بنفسہ کو سپر د کر نالازم ہوگا۔ بشرطیکہ مکفول لا کفیل سے اس وقت میں مطالبہ کرے تاکہ کفیل اس کو ادا کرے جس کا اس نے التزام کیا ہے۔ پس اگر کفیل نے ملکول بنفسہ کو وقت معینہ میں سپر د کر دیا تو فبہا کفیل بری الذمہ ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفیل
He said: If in kafalah bi al-nafs, the delivery of the makful bihi is conditioned at a specific time, it is necessary for him (the kafil) to bring him when he (the claimant) demands him at that time, fulfilling what he undertook. So if he brings him, [fine]; otherwise, the judge will imprison him because he has refrained from fulfilling a right due upon him. But the judge will not imprison him the first time, because perhaps he does not know why he is being sued. And if the makful bihi (the person guaranteed) is absent, the judge will give him a period of his (the makful bihi's) coming and going. If that period passes and he does not bring him, the judge will imprison him because his refusal to fulfill the right is confirmed.
Translation: Then if in kafalah bi al-nafs, the delivery of the makful bihi at a specific time is conditioned, then the kafil must bring the makful bihi. Provided that the makful lahu (claimant) demands him at that time, so that he fulfills what he undertook. So if the kafil brings him, then fine; otherwise, the judge will imprison him because he has refrained from fulfilling a right that is obligatory upon him. But the judge will not imprison him the first time, because perhaps he does not know why he is called. And if the makful bihi absents himself, the judge will give him a period for his travel and return. If the period passes and he could not bring him, the judge will imprison him because his refusal to fulfill the right is confirmed.
Explanation: The case is that if in kafalah bi al-nafs a specific time for delivery is conditioned, then it becomes necessary for the kafil to deliver the makful bihi at that specific time. Provided that the makful lahu demands him at that time so that the kafil fulfills what he undertook. So if the kafil delivers the makful bihi at the specific time, then fine, the kafil is free of liability. And if the kafil... (text ends).
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the effect of specifying a time in kafalah bi al-nafs. The matn states that if a specific time is stipulated, the kafil must produce the person when demanded within that time. Failure leads to imprisonment by the judge, but not on the first demand (to allow explanation). If the guaranteed person is absent, the judge grants a travel period. Only after that period, if still not produced, is the kafil imprisoned. The commentary explains that the obligation is conditional on the claimant's demand at the specified time. This ensures the kafil knows exactly when performance is due.

Key Terms
مکفول بہ (makful bihi): The person whose appearance or delivery is guaranteed in kafalah bi al-nafs.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The person in whose favor the guarantee is made; the one who demands the presence of the makful bihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a time-conditioned kafalah bi al-nafs obligates the kafil to produce the person only upon demand at that time, with a graduated enforcement process including investigation and travel allowance before imprisonment.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
10 min
Stipulating Delivery Time in Kafalah bi al-Nafs and Imprisonment of Guarantor
Details the ruling when a specific delivery time is stipulated in personal suretyship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a delivery time is stipulated in personal suretyship and explain the judge's procedure for imprisoning the guarantor, including the conditions of knowledge and ability.

Core Idea
In kafalah bi al-nafs, the guarantor is not imprisoned until he knows the reason and either refuses despite ability or fails after a grace period.

This passage from al-Hidayah details a nuanced ruling on personal suretyship. When a specific time is set for delivering the principal, the guarantor must produce him upon demand. However, the judge's imprisonment is not automatic; it depends on knowledge, ability, and the principal's whereabouts. Understanding this due process is essential for correctly applying the Hanafi ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the condition in kafalah bi al-nafs to deliver the principal (makful bihi) at a specified time. The ruling is that the guarantor must produce him at that time upon the creditor's demand.
This is a wajib obligation derived from the contract's terms.
2
Understand the judge's initial restraint
The judge does not imprison the guarantor immediately upon failure. First, he informs him of the reason because the guarantor might not know why he was summoned.
This is a key principle: imprisonment requires knowledge of the obligation.
3
Distinguish between scenarios after knowledge
Once the guarantor knows, two cases arise: he is able to produce but refuses (imprisoned), or he is unable because the principal is absent. If absent with known location, a grace period (travel time) is given; if still not produced, imprisoned.
Imprisonment is for refusal to fulfill a wajib right, not for inability.
4
Analyze the case of unknown whereabouts
If the principal's location is unknown, the demand may be dropped if both parties agree. If they dispute, the burden of proof determines whose word is accepted: if the principal's travel is known, the creditor's word is taken; otherwise the guarantor's.
This applies the principle that the defendant's statement prevails when the plaintiff lacks evidence.
5
Apply the due process framework
The passage establishes a stepwise procedure: judge summons → guarantor learns reason → if able but refuses → imprisoned; if unable and principal known → grace period → after that imprisoned; if unknown → dispute resolution via burden of proof.
This framework balances the creditor's right and the guarantor's fairness.

ہوگا اور مدعی کے پاس بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں چونکہ مدعی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ یعنی کفیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
He said: If a condition is stipulated in kafalah bi al-nafs to hand over the principal at a specific time, then it is necessary for him (the guarantor) to produce him when the creditor demands him at that time, fulfilling what he undertook. So if he produces him, (good). Otherwise, the judge shall imprison him because of his refusal to fulfill a right due upon him. But he shall not imprison him the first time, because perhaps he does not know why he is summoned. And if the principal goes absent, the judge shall give him a period equal to the time of going and coming. Then if that period passes and he does not produce him, the judge shall imprison him because his refusal to fulfill the right is confirmed. Translation: Then if in kafalah bi al-nafs a condition is made for handing over the principal at a specified time, it becomes necessary for the guarantor to produce the principal at that time, provided that the creditor demands it from the guarantor at that time so that he may fulfill what he undertook. So if the guarantor produces the principal at the specified time, then good, and the guarantor is discharged. But if the guarantor cannot produce the principal, the judge shall not order his arrest and imprisonment on the first instance, because it is very possible that the guarantor does not know why he has been summoned. And when the guarantor does not know why the judge has summoned him, he is not considered a wrongdoer in failing to produce the principal. And when the guarantor is not a wrongdoer, he will not be imprisoned, because imprisonment is the punishment for wrongdoing. If the guarantor comes to know that the judge has summoned him to produce the principal, but despite that he cannot produce him, there are two possibilities: either he is unable to produce him or he is able. If he is able but does not produce him, the judge shall imprison him, because the guarantor has stopped fulfilling a wajib right, and one who stops fulfilling a wajib right is a wrongdoer in the eyes of the Shari'ah, and the punishment for wrongdoing is imprisonment. And if the guarantor is unable to produce the principal, i.e., the principal has gone absent, then there are also two possibilities: the whereabouts of the principal are known or unknown. If known, the judge gives him a period to go and come back, i.e., enough time for the guarantor to go to where the principal is, meet him, bring him back, and return here. Then if this period passes and the guarantor cannot produce him, the judge will imprison him, because in this case too the guarantor has stopped fulfilling a wajib right, and stopping is wrongdoing, so he is imprisoned. If the whereabouts are unknown, then the creditor may either agree with the guarantor or disagree. If the creditor also says that the principal's whereabouts are truly unknown, then the demand from the guarantor is dropped for the time being. If the claim continues, the guarantor says he does not know, and the creditor says the guarantor does know, then if the principal's travel and business place is well known (people know he used to go to a certain place for trade etc.), then the creditor's statement is accepted, and the guarantor is ordered to go to that place. In this case, the apparent situation favors the creditor, so he becomes the defendant. Thus the creditor is the defendant, and the guarantor is the plaintiff; and it is assumed that the plaintiff has no evidence; when the plaintiff has no evidence, the defendant's statement is accepted. If the principal's travel place is not well known, then the guarantor's statement is accepted, because it agrees with the apparent situation and the original state, so the guarantor becomes the defendant, and the plaintiff (creditor) has no evidence, so the defendant's statement is accepted.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling on personal suretyship (kafalah bi al-nafs) when a specific delivery time is stipulated. It begins by stating the basic rule: if such a condition is made, the guarantor must deliver the principal at that time upon the creditor's demand. If he fails, the judge may imprison him, but not immediately—the judge first informs him of the reason. If the principal has fled, the judge grants a grace period equal to travel time. The commentary then elaborates on the conditions for imprisonment. The key distinction is knowledge: if the guarantor does not know why he was summoned, he is not a wrongdoer and not imprisoned. Once he knows, if he is able but refuses, he is imprisoned as a wrongdoer. If he is unable because the principal is absent, the judge grants a travel period. If after that he still cannot produce, he is imprisoned because he has failed to fulfill a wajib right. For an absent principal with unknown whereabouts, if both parties agree on the unknown status, the claim is suspended. If they dispute, and the principal's travel destination is known, the creditor's word is taken (he becomes defendant, guarantor plaintiff, and since plaintiff lacks evidence, defendant's word stands). If unknown, the guarantor's word is accepted (he becomes defendant). This entire discussion is based on the principles of wajib fulfillment, wrongdoing, imprisonment, and burden of proof.

Key Terms
کفالہ بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): A suretyship contract where the guarantor undertakes to produce the principal (the person himself) upon demand.
مکفول بہ (makful bihi): The principal for whom the guarantor undertakes; in kafalah bi al-nafs, it is the person himself.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor or person to whom the guarantor is obligated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Immediately after the time expires and the guarantor fails to produce
B) Only after the guarantor has been informed of the reason and has either refused despite ability or failed after a grace period
C) After the judge has confirmed the principal's absence
D) Only if the creditor demands imprisonment

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, imprisoning a guarantor under kafalah bi al-nafs requires due process: knowledge of the obligation, ability to produce, and a grace period if the principal is absent.

Kafalah — Surety

Imprisonment of the Guarantor: Conditions and Procedure
Ruling on when and how to imprison the guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a guarantor is imprisoned for failing to produce the principal and apply the evidentiary rules for disputes over the principal's whereabouts.

Core Idea
The guarantor is only imprisoned if he knowingly and willfully fails to produce the principal; incapacity suspends the demand.

This passage from the Hanafi school details the procedure for imprisoning a guarantor (kafil) who fails to bring the guaranteed person (makful bih) as ordered by the judge. It establishes that imprisonment is not automatic but depends on knowledge, capability, and the principal's whereabouts. The text also provides evidentiary rules when the location is disputed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline rule
The judge should not imprison the guarantor on the first summons because he may not know the reason.
This protects the guarantor from unjust punishment due to ignorance.
2
Determine if the guarantor is aware and capable
If the guarantor knows the summons reason and is able to produce the principal but fails, he is considered unjust (zalim) and is imprisoned.
Knowledge and capability are prerequisites for imprisonment.
3
Distinguish incapacity cases
If the guarantor is incapable because the principal is missing, check if the principal's whereabouts are known.
Two subcases: known whereabouts vs. unknown whereabouts.
4
Apply the grace period rule
If the whereabouts are known, the judge grants travel time; failure after that leads to imprisonment.
This gives the guarantor a chance to fulfill his duty.
5
Handle disputed whereabouts
If whereabouts are unknown and claimant disagrees, the judge looks to public knowledge: if the principal's travel is well-known, the claimant's word is accepted; otherwise, the guarantor's word is accepted.
The evidentiary rule shifts the burden based on apparent state.

یہ معلوم نہیں کہ حاکم نے کیوں طلب کیا ہے تو کفیل مکفول نفسہ کو سپرد نہ کرنے میں ظالم بھی نہ ہوگا۔ اور جب کفیل ظالم نہیں ٹھہرا تو اس کو قید بھی نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ قید میں ڈالنا ظالم کی سزا ہے۔ میں کفیل کو محبوس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفیل مکفول بنفسہ کو سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہے۔ بایں طور کہ مکفول بنفسہ غائب ہو گیا تو اس کی بھی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ مکفول بنفسہ کا ٹھکانا معلوم ہوگا یا اس کا ٹھکانا معلوم نہ ہوگا۔ اگر اول ہے تو حاکم اسکو آمد ورفت کی مدت تک مہلت دے گا۔ یعنی اتنی مدت مہلت دے گا کہ کفیل یہاں سے جائے اور مکفول نفسہ جہاں موجود ہے اس سے مل کر اس کو ساتھ لائے اور یہاں پہنچے ۔ پھر اگر یہ مدت گذرگئی اور کفیل مکفول بنفسہ کو حاضر نہ کر سکا تو اس صورت میں بھی کفیل کو محبوس کر دیا جائے گا۔ اسلئے کہ اس صورت میں بھی کفیل واجبی حق ادا کرنے سے رک گیا ہے۔ اور واجبی حق ادا کرنے سے رکنا چونکہ ظلم ہے اور ظلم کی سزا حبس اور قید ہے اسلئے اس صورت میں بھی کفیل کو قید خانہ میں ڈال دیا جائے گا اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی مکفول بنفسہ غائب ہے اور اس کا ٹھکانا معلوم نہیں ہے تو مکفول لہ اس سلسلہ میں کفیل کے موافق ہوگا یا مخالف ہو گا۔ اگر اول ہے یعنی مکفول لہ بھی کہتا ہے کہ واقعی مکفول بنفسہ کا ٹھکانا معلوم نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں کفیل سے فی الحال مطالبہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ یعنی جب تک مکفول بنفسہ کا ٹھکانا معلوم نہ ہو تو کفیل سے مطالبہ ساقط رہے گا کیونکہ اس صورت میں کفیل اور مکفول لہ دونوں فی الحال مکفول بنفسہ سپرد کرنے سے عاجز ہونے پر متفق ہیں اور اگر ثانی ہے یعنی کفیل کہتا ہے کہ مجھے اس کا ٹھکانا معلوم نہیں ہے اور مکفول لہ کہتا ہے کہ کفیل کو اس کا ٹھکانا معلوم ہے تو اگر مکفول بنفسہ کا نکلنا اور سفر کرنا معروف ہے یعنی لوگ جانتے ہیں کہ وہ فلاں جگہ تجارت وغیرہ کی غرض سے آتا جاتا رہتا تھا تو اس صورت میں مکفول لہ کا قول معتبر ہو گا اور کفیل کو اس جگہ جانے کا حکم کیا جائے گا جس جگہ کی لوگوں نے نشاندہی کی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں ظاہر حال مکفول لہ کے موافق ہے اور ظاہر حال جس کے موافق ہوتا ہے وہ مدعی علیہ ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے مکفول لہ مدعی علیہ ہوا اور جب مکفول لہ مدعی علیہ ہے تو کفیل مدعی ہو گا اور مسئلہ مفروضہ یہ ہے کہ مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہیں ہے اور جس وقت مدعی کے پاس بینہ موجود نہ ہو تو مدعی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ یعنی مکفول لہ کا قول معتبر ہوگا اور اگر مکفول بنفسہ کے نکلنے اور تجارت وغیرہ کے لئے جانے کی جگہ معروف نہ ہو تو کفیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں کفیل کا قول ظاہر حال اور اصل کے موافق ہے لہذا کفیل مدعی علیہ ہوگا اور مدعی کے پاس بینہ نہ ہونے کی صورت میں چونکہ مدعی علیہ کا قول معتبر ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے اس صورت میں مدعی علیہ یعنی کفیل کا قول معتبر ہو گا۔
Book of Kafalah
If he could not produce the guaranteed person, the judge should not order the guarantor to be arrested and put in prison on the first occasion. Because it is very possible that the guarantor did not even know why he was summoned. And when the guarantor does not know why the judge summoned him, then the guarantor is not unjust (zalim) in not handing over the principal. And when the guarantor is not deemed unjust, he will not be imprisoned, because imprisonment is the punishment of the unjust. If the guarantor did know that the judge summoned him to produce the principal but still could not produce him, then there are two cases: either he is incapable of producing him, or he is capable. If he is capable yet did not produce, the judge will imprison the guarantor, because the guarantor has refrained from fulfilling a wajib right, and one who refrains from fulfilling a wajib right is unjust in the eyes of the Shari'ah; the punishment for injustice is detention and imprisonment. Therefore in this case the guarantor will be imprisoned. If the guarantor is incapable of handing over the principal, for example the principal has disappeared, then there are also two cases: either the principal's whereabouts are known, or they are unknown. If the first, the judge will grant him time for travel and return, i.e., he will allow such time that the guarantor can go from here, meet the principal wherever he is, bring him back and arrive here. Then if this time passes and the guarantor could not produce the principal, then in this case also the guarantor will be imprisoned. Because in this case too the guarantor has refrained from fulfilling a wajib right, and refraining from fulfilling a wajib right is injustice, and the punishment for injustice is detention and imprisonment, so in this case too the guarantor will be thrown into prison. If the second, i.e., the principal is missing and his whereabouts are unknown, then the claimant (makful lahu) in this matter will either agree with the guarantor or disagree. If the first, i.e., the claimant also says, 'Indeed the principal's whereabouts are not known', then in this case the demand against the guarantor is dropped for the time being. That is, as long as the principal's whereabouts are not known, the demand against the guarantor remains dropped, because in this case both the guarantor and the claimant are in agreement that currently they are incapable of handing over the principal. If the second, i.e., the guarantor says 'I do not know his whereabouts' and the claimant says 'The guarantor knows his whereabouts', then if the principal's leaving and traveling is well-known, i.e., people know that he used to come and go to such-and-such place for trade etc., then in this case the claimant's statement will be accepted, and the guarantor will be ordered to go to that place which people have indicated. Because in this case the apparent state of affairs agrees with the claimant, and the one in whose favor the apparent state speaks is the defendant (mudda'a alayh). Therefore the claimant becomes the defendant, and when the claimant is the defendant, the guarantor becomes the plaintiff. The assumed case is that the plaintiff does not have evidence. And when the plaintiff does not have evidence, the defendant's statement is accepted. Hence in this case the defendant, i.e., the claimant's statement is accepted. And if the principal's leaving and the place for trade etc. are not well-known, then the guarantor's statement is accepted. Because in this case the guarantor's statement agrees with the apparent state and the original principle; hence the guarantor is the defendant, and when the plaintiff does not have evidence, the defendant's statement is accepted. Therefore in this case the defendant, i.e., the guarantor's statement is accepted.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the consequences for a guarantor (kafil) who fails to produce the guaranteed person (makful bih) as required by the judge. It opens by stating that on the first summons, the judge should not immediately imprison the guarantor because he might not know the reason. The guarantor is only considered unjust (zalim) and thus eligible for imprisonment if he knowingly and willfully refuses to produce the principal. The passage then provides a comprehensive breakdown: if the guarantor knows the summons but is able to produce, he must do so; otherwise he is imprisoned. If he is incapable due to the principal being missing, then further subcases arise. If the principal's location is known, the guarantor is given travel time; if he still fails, he is imprisoned for delaying. If the location is unknown, the key factor is whether the claimant agrees. If both agree the whereabouts are unknown, the demand is suspended. If they dispute, the judge looks to public knowledge: if the principal's whereabouts are commonly known, the claimant's word is taken (as defendant) and the guarantor must go; if not commonly known, the guarantor's word is accepted. This reflects Hanafi principles of justice and evidentiary rules.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): The guarantor who undertakes to produce the principal (makful bih) when required.
مكفول بنفسہ (makful bih): The person whose presence is guaranteed by the kafil.
مكفول لہ (makful lahu): The claimant (or beneficiary) who has the right to demand the presence of the principal.
ظالم (zalim): Unjust; a person who refrains from fulfilling a wajib obligation without excuse.
مهلت (muhlat): A grace period granted by the judge for the guarantor to travel and bring the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which condition is the guarantor immediately imprisoned?
A) When he fails to produce the principal on the first summons.
B) When he knows the reason for summons and is capable but does not produce.
C) When the principal's whereabouts are unknown and the claimant disagrees.
D) When the guarantor is incapable and the principal is missing.

Key Takeaway
The guarantor is only imprisoned for willful and capable refusal; incapacity suspends the demand, and disputes over whereabouts are resolved by public knowledge.

Guarantor's Liability When Principal Becomes Apostate
Ruling on the guarantor when the principal apostatizes and joins enemy territory

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the guarantor's liability when the guaranteed person apostatizes and joins enemy territory, explain the analogy to an insolvent debtor, and apply the rule regarding early delivery.

Core Idea
The guarantor is treated as incapable if the principal flees to Dar al-Harb; a treaty gives grace, no treaty absolves; term is the guarantor's right.

In Hanafi kafalah, the guarantor must produce the principal. What happens if the principal becomes an apostate and escapes to enemy lands? This lesson from al-Hidayah uses qiyas to the insolvent debtor and clarifies how the guarantor's right to the term affects liability, distinguishing between accessible and inaccessible territories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Note the specific case: the guaranteed person (makful bih) apostatizes and flees to Dar al-Harb. The initial ruling: the guarantor is considered 'incapable' and given a grace period.
The ruling is from al-Quduri and explained in al-Hidayah.
2
Locate the dalil (analogy)
The text states this is like the case of an insolvent debtor (kaladhi a'sara). The common illa is incapacity to fulfill the obligation.
Qiyas is used; the illa is temporary or permanent incapacity.
3
Distinguish the two subcases
If a treaty exists allowing travel, the guarantor gets a grace period to retrieve the principal; failure leads to imprisonment. If no treaty, the guarantor is completely incapable and absolved.
The treaty determines accessibility.
4
Analyze the effect of early delivery
If the guarantor hands over the principal before the term, he is absolved because the term (ajal) is his right and he can waive it.
Analogous to a debtor paying a deferred debt early.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools consider the term as the creditor's right, not the guarantor's, which would affect the validity of early delivery.
Hanafis uniquely hold the term as the guarantor's right, allowing waiver.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكفول بنفسہ شخص مرتد ہو گیا العیاذ باللہ اور دارالحرب میں لاحق ہو گیا تو کفیل اتنی مدت گویا عاجز ہے اسے مہلت دی جائے گی
قال وكذا اذا ارتد والعياذ بالله ولحق بدار الحرب وهذا لانه عاجز فى المدة فينظر كالذي اعسر ولو سلمه قبل ذلك برى لان الاجل حقه فيملک اسقاطه كمــا فــي الــديــن الـمـؤجل
ترجمہ اور اسی طرح اگر مکفول بنفسہ نعوذ باللہ منہ مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں لاحق ہو گیا اور یہ اسلئے کہ کفیل اتنی مدت تک عاجز ہے لہذا اس کو مہلت دی جائے گی۔ جیسے اس شخص کو جو تنگدست ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر کفیل نے مکفول بنفسہ کو وقت معینہ سے پہلے سپرد کر دیا تو بری ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ میعاد کفیل کا حق ہے لہذا وہ اس کو ساقط کرنے کا بھی مالک ہے جیسے ادھار قرضہ میں ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر مکفول بنفسہ مرتد ہو کر دار الحرب میں چلا گیا اور دارالحرب والوں سے دارالاسلام والوں کا آمد ورفت کے سلسلہ میں یہ معاہدہ ہے کہ وہ ہمارے یہاں آسکتے ہیں اور ہم دار الحرب جا سکتے ہیں ۔ تو ایسی صورت میں بھی کفیل کو آمد ورفت کی مدت تک کیلئے مہلت دی جائے گی۔ اگر اس مدت میں لا کر حاضر کر دیا تو سبحان اللہ ورنہ کفیل کو جیل خانہ پہنچا دیا جائے گا۔ اور اس صورت میں مہلت اسلئے دی گئی کہ کفیل اتنی مدت تک عاجز ہے اور عاجز کو مہلت دی جاتی ہے۔ اسلئے کفیل کو اتنی مدت مہلت دی گئی ہے۔ جیسا کہ قرضدار کے قرضہ کی ادائیگی کا کوئی وعدہ ہومگر وہ اپنی تنگدستی کی وجہ سے ایسا ہو گیا کہ قرضہ ادا نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کو فراخی کے وقت تک مہلت دی جاتی ہے۔ پس اسی طرح مذکورہ صورت میں چونکہ کفیل بھی عاجز ہے اسلئے آمد ورفت کی مدت تک اس کو مہلت دی جائے گی ۔
اور اگر دار الحرب اور دار الاسلام کے درمیان اس طرح کا کوئی معاہدہ نہ ہو تو کفیل چونکہ اس صورت میں بالکل عاجز ہے۔ اسلئے اس سے اب کوئی مواخذہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ اور اگر کفیل نے مکفول بنفسہ کو وقت معینہ سے پہلے سپرد کر دیا تو کفیل بری ہو جائے گا کیونکہ میعاد کفیل کا حق ہے اور ہر صاحب حق کو چونکہ اپنا حق ساقط کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا ہے۔ اسلئے کفیل کو بھی اپنا حق میعاد ساقط کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا جیسے میعادی ادھار میں ہے کہ اگر قرضدار نے مدت سے پہلے ادا کر دیا تو قرضدار بری ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مدت اس کا حق تھا۔ پس اسی طرح کفالہ میں بھی مدت مذکور چونکہ کفیل کا حق ہے اسلئے مدت سے پہلے ادا کرنے سے بری ہو جائے گا۔
If the guaranteed person became an apostate – God forbid – and joined Dar al-Harb, then the guarantor is during that period considered incapable; he will be given a grace period.
He (al-Quduri) said: Similarly, if he apostatizes – God forbid – and joins Dar al-Harb, this is because he is incapable during that period, so he is treated like one who has become insolvent. And if he handed him over before that time, he is absolved, because the term is his right, so he has the power to drop it, as in the case of a deferred debt.
Translation and similarly if the guaranteed person – we seek refuge in Allah from him – becomes an apostate and joins Dar al-Harb; and this is because the guarantor is incapable during that period, therefore he will be given a grace period, like the person who has become insolvent. And if the guarantor handed over the guaranteed person before the appointed time, he is absolved, because the term is the guarantor's right, therefore he has the right to drop it, as happens in a deferred loan.
Explanation: The author of al-Hidayah says: If the guaranteed person becomes an apostate and goes to Dar al-Harb, and between the people of Dar al-Harb and the people of Dar al-Islam there is a treaty allowing travel and coming and going – i.e., they can come to us and we can go to Dar al-Harb – then in such a case also the guarantor will be given a grace period for travel and return. If he brings him and hands him over within that time, good; otherwise the guarantor will be sent to prison. The grace period is given because the guarantor is incapable during that period, and the incapable one is given a grace period. So the guarantor is given that time. Just as if a debtor had a promise to repay a debt but due to his indigence he cannot repay, he is given a grace period until ease. So similarly, in the mentioned situation, since the guarantor is also incapable, he will be given a grace period for travel and return. And if there is no such treaty between Dar al-Harb and Dar al-Islam, then the guarantor is completely incapable in this case, so he will not be held accountable at all. And if the guarantor handed over the guaranteed person before the appointed time, the guarantor becomes absolved, because the term is the guarantor's right, and every holder of a right has the authority to drop his right. Hence the guarantor will have the authority to drop his right to the term, as in the case of a deferred loan: if the debtor pays before the term, the debtor becomes absolved, because the term was his right. In the same way, in kafalah, the mentioned term is the guarantor's right, so by handing over before the term he becomes absolved.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling from the Hanafi school on the situation when the guaranteed person (makful bih) becomes an apostate and flees to enemy territory (Dar al-Harb). It begins with the principle that the guarantor is considered incapable during the period until he can retrieve him, so he is given a grace period by analogy with an insolvent debtor who cannot pay. The main Arabic text from al-Quduri states this, and the commentary expands. The commentary by the author of al-Hidayah (صاحب ہدایہ) clarifies: if there is a treaty between the two territories allowing travel, the guarantor is given time to travel and bring him back; if he fails after that, he is imprisoned because he becomes able after the travel period. If no such treaty exists, the guarantor is completely incapable and is not held liable at all. Additionally, the passage discusses that if the guarantor hands over the principal before the agreed term, he is absolved because the term is his right and he can waive it, similar to a debtor paying off a deferred debt early. This ruling reflects Hanafi legal reasoning using qiyas (analogy) and the concept of haqq (right) of the guarantor.

Key Terms
ارتد (irtadda): To apostatize from Islam; here, the guaranteed person leaves Islam and joins enemy territory.
دار الحرب (dar al-harb): Territory under non-Muslim control with which there is no peace treaty.
أجل (ajal): The term or deadline for handing over the principal; it is considered the right of the guarantor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, what happens if the guaranteed person apostatizes and goes to Dar al-Harb but there is no treaty allowing travel between the two territories?
A) The guarantor is given a grace period to travel.
B) The guarantor is imprisoned immediately.
C) The guarantor is completely absolved of liability.
D) The guarantor must pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
The guarantor's liability depends on his ability to retrieve the principal; if incapable due to the principal's flight to inaccessible territory, he is absolved, and the term is his right to waive.

Delivery in a Litigable Place Absolves the Guarantor
Ruling that delivery in a litigable place absolves the guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a guarantor is absolved and apply it to a scenario.

Core Idea
Guarantor is absolved by making the principal available for litigation, not by physical handover alone.

In Hanafi fiqh of kafalah, the guarantor's obligation is to produce the principal for legal proceedings. This lesson clarifies that if the guarantor brings the principal to a place where the claimant can sue—like within the city—the obligation is discharged, even if no physical handover occurs. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion about what constitutes fulfillment of the guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The guarantor's obligation is to produce the principal (makful bih) to enable litigation. The act is the delivery or presentation of the principal to a place where the claimant can initiate a lawsuit.
This is not about physical handover to the claimant; it is about enabling legal contestation.
2
Identify the condition
The condition for absolution is that the delivery must occur in a place where the claimant (makful lahu) is able to litigate (mukhasamah) against the principal. Typically this means a place with an accessible judge, such as a city court.
The text gives the example of 'within the city' as a sufficient place.
3
Determine the ruling
If the condition is met, the guarantor is absolved (bari') from the guarantee. The reason is that he has fulfilled the purpose of his undertaking, which is to enable the claimant to pursue his claim legally.
The ruling is based on the principle that the substance of the obligation matters more than the form.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكفول بہ کو ایسی جگہ حاضر کیا کہ مکفول لہ کو مخاصمت پر قدرت ہو تو کیا حکم ہے؟
قال : وإذا أحضره وسلمه فى مكان يقدر المكفول له ان يخاصمه فيه مثل ان يكون في مصر برى الكفيل من الكفالة لانه اتى بما التزمه وحصل المقصود به ولهذا لانه ما التزم التسليم الامرة
ترجمہ اور اگر کفیل نے اس کو لا کر ایسی جگہ سپرد کیا جہاں مکفول لہ کو اس کے ساتھ خصومت کی قدرت ہے جیسے شہر کے اندر ہو تو کفیل، کفالہ سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے جو کچھ التزام کیا تھا وہ پورا کر دیا اور ایسا کرنے سے مقصود حاصل ہو جاتا ہے اور یہ اسلئے کہ کفیل
If he brings the guaranteed person and hands him over in a place where the claimant is able to litigate against him, for example within the city, then the guarantor is absolved from the guarantee, because he has fulfilled what he undertook and the purpose is achieved. And this is because he did not undertake the delivery except [for the purpose of litigation?].
Translation: And if the guarantor brought him and handed him over in a place where the claimant has the ability to litigate with him, like within the city, then the guarantor is absolved from the guarantee. Because he has done what he undertook, and the purpose is achieved by doing so. And this is because the guarantor... [text cuts off]
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school on the sufficient manner of discharging the guarantee. The guarantor (kafil) is obliged to produce the principal (makful bih) to the claimant (makful lahu). The question is: if the guarantor brings the principal to a place where the claimant is able to initiate legal proceedings (mukhasama) against him, such as within the city where the court is accessible, is this sufficient? The ruling from the matn (al-Quduri) states that if the guarantor hands over the principal in such a place, he is absolved (bari') of the guarantee. The reason is that the obligation (iltizam) of the guarantor is not to deliver the principal to a specific location but to enable the claimant to pursue his claim. If the claimant can legally contest the principal in that place, the objective of the guarantee is achieved. The commentary emphasizes this by stating that the guarantor has fulfilled what he undertook, and the purpose is thereby attained. Note that the Arabic text is cut off at the end, but the translation and commentary complete the sense. This ruling highlights the principle that the substance of the obligation matters more than the form.

Key Terms
مخاصمت (mukhasamah): Legal litigation or contestation; the ability to sue the principal in court.
برئ (bari'): Absolved, released from the obligation of the guarantee.
التزم (iltazama): To undertake an obligation; the guarantor undertook to make the principal available.
كفالة (kafalah): Guarantee; a contract where one person (kafil) undertakes to produce another (makful bih) to answer a claim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the guarantor absolved from the guarantee?
A) Only when he hands over the principal to the judge.
B) When he hands over the principal in a place where the claimant can litigate against him.
C) Only when he hands over the principal inside the court building.
D) When the claimant acknowledges receipt.

Key Takeaway
The guarantor is absolved when he makes the principal available for litigation in a proper place, not necessarily by physical handover.

Discharge of the Surety by Delivering the Principal Where Litigation is Possible
Ruling with rationale and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on discharge of a personal surety (kafalah bi al-nafs) and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the locality of delivery.

Core Idea
The surety is discharged when the principal is delivered in any place where the creditor can sue him—the purpose is to enable litigation.

In personal suretyship (kafalah bi al-nafs), the surety guarantees the presence of the debtor for litigation. This lesson examines the condition under which the surety is discharged from his obligation: delivering the principal in a location where the creditor can legally bring a claim. The passage from al-Hidayah presents the ruling and its rationale, and then notes an important difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Sahibayn) on whether the delivery must be in the same city where the suretyship was contracted. Understanding this dispute clarifies the practical scope of the surety's liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the surety delivering the principal debtor to a place. The ruling is that the surety is discharged (bari') from the suretyship obligation.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the creditor accepts delivery; the mere ability to sue is sufficient.
2
Identify the condition for discharge
The place must be one where the creditor can litigate against the principal (e.g., a city with a judge). This is the only condition mentioned.
If the place lacks a judge or legal system, the purpose of litigation is not possible, and the surety is not discharged.
3
Understand the rationale (talil)
The surety has fulfilled his undertaking (iltizam) and the purpose (maqsud) of kafalah—enabling litigation—is achieved. The surety only undertook to deliver once.
This reasoning shows that the ruling is based on the objective of the contract, not just literal performance.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that delivery in any city suffices. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require delivery in the same city where the suretyship was contracted.
The dispute centers on whether the obligation is tied to the original forum or to the general purpose of litigation.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a surety in Cairo who delivers the debtor in Alexandria, where the creditor can sue. According to Abu Hanifa, he is discharged; according to Sahibayn, he is not.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) depends on which view is followed in fatwa.

He said: And if he brings him and delivers him in a place where the creditor can litigate against him, such as being in a city, the surety is discharged from the suretyship because he has fulfilled what he undertook and the purpose is achieved, and because he only undertook to deliver once. Translation: And if the surety brings him and delivers him in a place where the creditor has the power to litigate against him, like inside the city, then the surety is discharged from the suretyship... Commentary: The scenario is: if the surety brings the principal person and delivers him in a place where the creditor can litigate and sue him, e.g., inside the city, the surety is discharged, whether the creditor accepts or not, because the purpose of personal suretyship is litigation in the judge's court. When the surety delivers in such a place, the purpose is achieved. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the delivery must be in the same city where the surety was made; according to Imam Abu Hanifa, any city suffices.

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with its rationale. The suretyship by person (kafalah bi al-nafs) aims to enable the creditor to bring the debtor to court. If the surety produces the debtor in any location where the creditor can legally sue him (e.g., a city with a judge), the purpose is fulfilled and the surety is discharged. The ruling does not require the creditor's acceptance; the mere ability to sue is sufficient. The commentary then notes an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Imam Abu Hanifa holds that delivery in any city is valid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) require delivery in the same city where the suretyship contract was made. The text does not specify which is mufta bihi here, but the general Hanafi position often follows the Sahibayn in matters of locality.

Key Terms
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor or beneficiary who is owed the presence of the principal person.
مخاصمت (mukhasamat): Litigation; the ability to bring a legal claim against the principal before a judge.

The surety's discharge in kafalah bi al-nafs hinges on enabling litigation; the locality requirement differs among Hanafi imams.

Ruling on Delivery in Market vs. Judge's Assembly
Discusses a conditional suretyship with a ruling shift based on social circumstances.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi ruling on conditional suretyship changed from early to later scholars and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A surety is discharged only if the condition fulfills the purpose; in corrupt times, market delivery fails.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh of kafalah addresses a nuanced scenario: a surety explicitly promises to deliver the principal debtor in the judge's assembly, but instead delivers him in the market. The early authorities ruled the surety discharged because the creditor can still litigate. However, later scholars reversed this in corrupt times, holding that the condition is essential. Understanding this shift illustrates how Hanafi law adapts to changing social circumstances ('urf and zaman) while preserving the underlying legal objective.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Condition and the Delivery
The surety stipulated delivery in the judge's assembly (majlis al-qadi). He delivered the principal in the market. Note the explicit condition.
2
Understand the Early Ruling and its Rationale
The early authorities said the surety is discharged because the purpose (power to litigate) is still achievable—the creditor can take the principal to court from the market.
The basis: 'bari' li-husul al-maqsud' (discharged due to purpose achieved).
3
Identify the Later Scholars' Objection
Later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) argued that in corrupt times, delivering in the market is ineffective. Bystanders would help the principal resist, preventing the creditor from bringing him to court.
The condition becomes essential (mufeed) in a corrupt environment.
4
Apply the Changed Circumstances (Zaman and 'Urf)
The later ruling is based on the reality of widespread corruption. The mufta bihi (operative fatwa) is that the surety is not discharged if he delivers elsewhere, as the condition is no longer superfluous.
This shows the Hanafi school's responsiveness to social context.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi and its Authority
The text states 'qila fi zamanina la yabru'—the later view is the relied-upon position. It is from the fatwa category of the mutakhkhirin, reflecting later Hanafi practice.
The early ruling remains valid in a just environment.

Source Text

واذا كفل على ان يسلمه فى مجلس القاضى فسلمه فى السوق برى لحصول المقصود وقيل في زماننا لا يبر ألان الظاهر المعاونة على الامتناع لا على الاحضار فكان التقييد مفيدا
ترجمہ اور اگر اس شرط پر کفیل ہوا کہ وہ اس کو قاضی کی مجلس میں سپر د کرے گا پھر اس شخص نے اس کو بازار میں سپر د کر دیا تو بری ہو گیا کیونکہ مقصود حاصل ہو گیا ہے اور کہا گیا کہ ہمارے زمانہ میں بری نہیں ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ ظاہر یہ ہے کہ (لوگ اس کو ) چھڑانے پر معاونت کریں گے نہ کہ حاضر کرنے پر اسلئے مجلس قاضی کی قید لگانا مفید ہوگا۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کوئی شخص اس شرط پر کفیل ہوا کہ میں مکفول بنفسہ کو قاضی کی مجلس میں سپر د کروں گا لیکن اس نے اس کو بازار میں مکفول لڑ کے سپر د یا تو کفیل برمی ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مکفول لہ کا مقصود یعنی قدرت علی المحاکمہ حاصل ہے کہ مکفول لۂ اس کو قاضی کے پاس لے جا کر اس سے مخاصمہ اور محاکمہ کر سکتا ہے۔ علمائے متاخرین نے کہا ہے کہ ہمارے زمانے میں مجلس قاضی کے علاوہ بازار وغیرہ میں سپرد کرنے سے کفیل بری نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ آج کل فسق و فجور اور فساد کا زمانہ ہے۔ لہذا اگر کفیل نے مجلس قاضی کے علاوہ بازار وغیرہ میں مکفول بنفسہ کو مکغول لڑ کے حوالہ کیا اور مکفول بنفسہ شور مچانے لگا اور اپنی مظلومیت کا اظہار کرنے لگا تو لوگ اس کو چھڑانے میں مددگار ہو جائیں گے اور مکفول لہ کی اس بارے میں کوئی مدد نہ کرے گا کہ مکفول بنفسہ کو قاضی کی عدالت میں حاضر کیا جائے تا کہ مکفول لا اپنے حق کے سلسلہ میں اس سے مخاصمہ کر سکے۔ پس جب یہ بات ہے تو مکفول بنفسہ کی حاضری کو مجلس قاضی کے ساتھ مقید کرنا مفید ہوگا ۔ اور جب مجلس قاضی کے ساتھ مقید کرنا مفید ہے تو مجلس قاضی میں حاضری کی شرط کے ساتھ مجلس قاضی کے علاوہ میں حاضر کرنا معتبر نہ ہوگا اور اس سے کفیل بری نہ ہوگا۔
And if he becomes surety on condition that he delivers him in the judge's assembly, then he delivers him in the market, he is discharged because the purpose is achieved. And it is said that in our time he is not discharged because it is apparent that people will help him [the principal] to resist, not to appear, so the restriction (to the judge's assembly) is beneficial. Translation: The issue: if a person becomes surety on the condition that he will deliver the principal in the judge's assembly, but he delivers him in the market, the surety is discharged because the purpose is achieved. And it is said that in our time he is not discharged because today people would help the principal resist and not assist in bringing him to court, so the condition of the judge's assembly is meaningful. Commentary: The later scholars (mutakhkhirin) said that in our time, delivering elsewhere does not discharge the surety because of widespread corruption; the principal would create a scene and people would help him escape, so the stipulation of the judge's assembly is essential.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage addresses a conditional suretyship: the surety explicitly promised to deliver the principal in front of the judge (majlis al-qadi). If he delivers in the market instead, the original ruling (of the early authorities) says he is discharged because the creditor can still take the principal to court from the market—the ability to litigate is achieved. However, the later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) revised this ruling based on changed social circumstances: in times of corruption and lawlessness, delivering in the market is ineffective because the principal may resist and bystanders might assist him to escape, preventing the creditor from bringing him to court. Therefore, the specific condition of the judge's assembly is now considered beneficial and must be observed; otherwise, the surety is not discharged. This shows how Hanafi fiqh adapts to changing times ('urf and zaman) while preserving the underlying objective of securing the principal's presence in court.

Key Terms
مجلس القاضى (majlis al-qadi): The judge's court or assembly; the place where legal proceedings are conducted.
علمائے متاخرین (ulama' al-mutakhkhirin): Later scholars of the Hanafi school who issued fatwas considering contemporary circumstances.
مقصود (maqsud): Purpose or objective; here, the ability of the creditor to bring the principal to court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the condition is invalid if not fulfilled to the letter.
B) Because people would help the principal resist, preventing the creditor from bringing him to court.
C) Because the market is not a proper place for legal delivery.
D) Because the creditor might not accept the delivery.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, conditional suretyship rulings may shift based on 'urf and zaman; the later mutakhkhirin fatwa that the surety is not discharged in corrupt times is the operative position.

Delivery Location and Surety Discharge in Kafalah
Rulings on delivery location for surety discharge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for discharge of a kafil bil-nafs and apply them to different delivery locations, including resolving the intra-Hanafi dispute on delivery in a different city.

Core Idea
Surety is discharged only if the creditor can sue the principal in the delivery location.

This passage from al-Hidayah examines when a surety for the person (kafil bil-nafs) is released from his obligation by delivering the principal (makful bihi) to the creditor. The key criterion is the creditor's ability to legally pursue his claim. The rulings vary by location: delivery in uninhabited areas or villages without a judge does not discharge, delivery in a different city is disputed between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and delivery in a prison not controlled by the creditor does not discharge. Understanding these nuances prevents incorrect fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the purpose of kafalah bil-nafs
The surety's obligation is to produce the principal so the creditor can sue him. The discharge occurs when the purpose is achieved.
The purpose (maqsad) is ability to sue (mukhasama).
2
Identify the four delivery scenarios
The text specifies: desert, village (sawad), different city (misr akhar), and prison.
Each scenario tests the ability to sue.
3
Apply the ability-to-sue test to desert and village
In desert no court exists; in village no judge. Creditor cannot sue, so surety not discharged.
Both fail the test.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf for different city
Abu Hanifa: any city with a judge suffices. Sahibayn: original city required because witnesses may be there.
Ikhtilaf rooted in factual assumptions about judicial reliability.
5
Evaluate the prison scenario
If imprisoned by someone other than creditor, creditor cannot sue, so no discharge. If imprisoned by creditor, discharge likely.
The text only mentions non-creditor imprisonment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان سلمه في برية لم يبرأ لأنه لا يقدر على المخاصمة فيها فلم يحصل المقصود وكذا إذا سلمه في سواد لعدم قاض يفصل الحكم فيه ولو سلم في مصر آخر غير المصر الذي كفل فيه برى عند أبي حنيفة للقدرة على المخاصمة فيه وعندهما لا يبرأ لأنه قد يكون شهوده فيما عينه ولو سلمه في السجن وقد حبسه غير الطالب لا يبرأ لأنه لا يقدر على المخاصمة فيه.
If he hands him over in a wilderness, he is not discharged because he (the creditor) cannot sue him there, so the purpose is not achieved. Likewise if he hands him over in a village due to absence of a judge to decide the case. If he hands him over in a city other than the city where he became surety, he is discharged according to Abu Hanifa due to ability to sue there, but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) he is not discharged because his witnesses may be in the city he specified. If he hands him over in a prison while someone other than the claimant had imprisoned him, he is not discharged because he cannot sue him there.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the discharge of a surety for the person (kafil bil-nafs) when he delivers the principal (makful bihi) to the creditor (makful lahu) in different locations. The key principle is that the surety is discharged only if the creditor can legally pursue his claim against the principal in that location. Delivery in an uninhabited area (bariyyah) or a village (sawad) without a judge does not discharge the surety, as the creditor cannot sue. For delivery in a different city, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa holds it sufficient because the creditor can sue in any city's court, while the Sahibayn require delivery in the original city because the creditor's witnesses might be there. Some later scholars explain this difference as contextual: in Abu Hanifa's time, judges were trustworthy and fair, so any city's court would do; later, as corruption spread, it became necessary to restrict delivery to the contracted city. Finally, if the principal is handed over in prison but imprisoned by someone other than the creditor, the surety is not discharged because the creditor cannot access him for litigation. However, if the principal was imprisoned by the creditor himself, the surety would be discharged (not mentioned in the Arabic but noted in the Urdu commentary).

Key Terms
مکفول بنفسہ (makful bihi): The principal debtor or person for whom surety is given (suretyship for the person).
کفیل بالنفس (kafil bil-nafs): The surety who guarantees the presence of a person (the principal).
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor or beneficiary of the suretyship who has a claim against the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The surety is discharged.
B) The surety is not discharged.
C) It depends on the judge.
D) The surety must pay a fine.

Key Takeaway
The surety's discharge depends on the creditor's ability to sue; location and judicial capacity are decisive.

Death Discharges the Surety for Person
Rulings on discharge due to death of parties in suretyship for person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of death in kafalah bil-nafs and explain the rationale (talil) distinguishing it from kafalah bil-mal.

Core Idea
Death of the principal or surety ends kafalah bil-nafs because it is a personal obligation, unlike financial suretyship.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi school on suretyship for person (kafalah bil-nafs). The key distinction is whether the obligation is personal or financial. The source text explains why death discharges the surety, while contrasting with kafalah bil-mal. Understanding this rationale is essential for correctly applying suretyship rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rulings
The text states three situations: death of principal discharges surety; death of surety discharges him; death of creditor transfers rights to his executor or heirs.
Focus on the discharge in first two cases.
2
Extract the rationale (talil)
The reason given: inability to produce the principal (due to death) and the personal nature of the obligation (surety cannot delegate to his property).
This is the core legal reasoning.
3
Distinguish from kafalah bil-mal
The text explicitly contrasts: 'unlike the surety for debt.' The difference is that financial obligations can be fulfilled from the estate.
This distinction is crucial for applying the correct ruling.
4
Note the scope of ikhtilaf
The commentary indicates that Imam Ahmad and one narration of Imam Shafi'i agree with the Hanafi position, implying other views may exist but are not detailed here.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: وإذا مات المكفول به برى الكفيل بالنفس من الكفالة لأنه عجز عن احضاره ولأنه سقط الحضور عن الأصيل فيسقط الإحضار به عن الكفيل وكذا إذا مات الكفيل لأنه لم يبق قادرا على تسليم المكفول بنفسه وماله لا يصلح لأداء لهذا الواجب بخلاف الكفيل بالمال ولو مات المكفول له فللوصي أن يطالب الكفيل وإن لم يكن فلوارثه لقيامه مقام الميت.
He said: When the principal (makful bihi) dies, the surety for the person is discharged from the suretyship because he is unable to produce him, and because the obligation of presence falls from the principal, so the obligation to produce him falls from the surety. Likewise, when the surety dies, because he is no longer able to hand over the principal himself, and his property is not fit for fulfilling this obligation, unlike the surety for debt. If the creditor (makful lahu) dies, his executor may claim from the surety, and if there is no executor, then his heir, as they stand in the place of the deceased.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage explains when kafalah bil-nafs ends. Death of the principal (makful bihi) discharges the surety because the purpose is to produce the principal, which is now impossible. The obligation to appear falls from the principal, and thus the surety's obligation to produce him also falls. Death of the surety himself also discharges him because this is a personal obligation that cannot be fulfilled by his estate, unlike kafalah bil-mal (suretyship for debt) where the surety's estate remains liable. The Urdu commentary adds that Imam Ahmad and one narration of Imam Shafi'i agree. If the creditor (makful lahu) dies, his right transfers to his executor or heirs, so the surety remains liable to them. The reasoning is that kafalah bil-nafs depends on the existence of both the surety and the principal.

Key Terms
کفیل بالنفس (kafil bil-nafs): Surety for the person, who guarantees to produce the principal.
مکفول بہ (makful bihi): The principal whose presence is guaranteed.
کفیل بالمال (kafil bil-mal): Surety for debt, who guarantees payment of a financial obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the difference between kafalah bil-nafs and kafalah bil-mal regarding the death of the surety?
A) Both end with the surety's death.
B) Neither ends.
C) Kafalah bil-nafs ends but kafalah bil-mal continues with the estate.
D) Kafalah bil-mal ends but kafalah bil-nafs continues.

Key Takeaway
Death of the principal or the surety terminates kafalah bil-nafs due to the personal nature of the obligation, distinguishing it from financial suretyship.

Kafalah — Surety

Death of Parties Discharges Personal Surety
Ruling with rational proof on discharge of personal surety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on discharge of personal surety upon death of any party and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) based on the subsidiary nature of the obligation.

Core Idea
Personal suretyship ends when the surety or debtor dies because the obligation is personal, not monetary.

This lesson examines the effect of death on a contract of personal suretyship (kafala bi al-nafs). The classical Hanafi position, as set forth in Al-Hidayah, is that death of either the principal debtor or the surety discharges the surety. The proof is rational: the surety's obligation is subsidiary to the debtor's duty to appear, and property cannot substitute for the personal act of delivery. This stands in contrast to a surety for debt, where the obligation survives because property can deputize.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage covers three possible deaths: the principal debtor (makful bih), the surety (kafil), and the creditor (makful lahu). For each, determine the legal consequence.
2
Extract the ruling for each
For debtor's death: surety discharged. For surety's death: surety discharged. For creditor's death: surety remains liable to the creditor's executor or heir.
3
Analyze the rational proof
Two proofs: (1) both parties must be alive for the obligation to continue; (2) the surety's obligation is subsidiary (tabi) to the debtor's obligation to appear, so when the debtor's obligation falls, the surety's falls.
This is a rational (aqli) proof, not textual.
4
Contrast with surety for debt
Unlike personal suretyship, a surety for debt is not discharged by death because property can stand in for the obligation and can be taken from the estate.

قال: وإذا مات المكفول به برى الكفيل بالنفس من الكفالة لانه عجز عن احضارة ولا نه سقط الحضور عن الاصيل فيسقط الاحضار به عن الكفيل وكذا اذامات الكفيل لانه لم يبق قادرا على تسليم المكفول بنفسه وماله لا يصلح لايفاء لهذا الواجب بخلاف الكفيل بالمال ولو مات المكفول له فللوصى ان يطالب الكفيل وان لم يكن فلوارثه لقيامه مقام الميت
