وقت ہی مال کا وصف بھی بیان کر دیا تھا۔ اور جب دعوی کرتے وقت مال کا وصف بھی بیان کر دیا گیا تو مال یعنی مدعی یہ مجہول نہ رہا اور جب مدعی یہ مجہول نہ رہا تو دعوی مال صحیح ہو گیا اور جب مال کا دعوی صحیح ہو گیا تو کفیل پر مکفول بنفسہ یعنی قرضدار کو حاضر کرنا بھی واجب ہو گیا اور جب کفیل پر مکفول بنفسم کو حاضر کرنا واجب ہو گیا تو کفالہ بانفس بھی صحیح ہو گیا اور جب کفالہ بالنفس صحیح ہو گیا تو کفالہ بالہال جو اس پر مرتب ہے وہ بھی صحیح ہو جائے گا۔ پس امام محمد کا یہ فرمانا کہ اگر دعویٰ کرتے وقت قرض خواہ نے مال کا وصف بیان نہ کیا تو کفالہ بالمال اور کفالہ بالنفس صحیح نہ ہوگا، غلط ہے۔
He had also described the property at the time. And when the property was described at the time of claim, the property, i.e., the thing claimed, did not remain unknown. And when the thing claimed was not unknown, the claim for property became valid. And when the claim for property became valid, it became obligatory upon the guarantor to produce the person guaranteed (the debtor). And when it became obligatory upon the guarantor to produce the person guaranteed, the suretyship for the person also became valid. And when the suretyship for the person became valid, the suretyship for the property which is attached to it also becomes valid. So Imam Muhammad's saying that if the creditor did not describe the property at the time of claim, then the suretyship for property and suretyship for person are not valid is incorrect.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute refuting Imam Muhammad's position on the necessity of describing the property at the time of filing a claim in a kafalah (suretyship) contract. The author presents a logical chain: when the creditor describes the property at the time of claim, the property becomes known (ma'lum), making the claim valid. A valid claim for property then obligates the guarantor (kafil) to produce the debtor (makful bih) in court, which constitutes a valid kafalah bi al-nafs. Consequently, the associated kafalah bi al-mal is also valid. Therefore, Imam Muhammad's view that describing the property is a condition for validity is rejected. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that describing the property at the time of claim is not a prerequisite; the claim is valid if the property is described at any point during the lawsuit.

Key Terms
كفالة بالمال (kafalah bi al-mal): A suretyship contract guaranteeing the payment of a debt or delivery of property.
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): A suretyship contract guaranteeing the presence of a person (debtor) before the court.
وصف (wasf): Description of the property that removes ignorance (jahl) about the subject matter.
معلوم (ma'lum): Known; certain knowledge that eliminates jahl (ignorance) about the subject matter.
جهل (jahl): Ignorance; uncertainty that can invalidate contracts if it pertains to essential terms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the direct consequence of describing the property at the time of claim?
A) The property becomes known, making the property claim valid.
B) The guarantor is immediately released from obligation.
C) The kafalah becomes invalid if description was not given earlier.
D) The debtor is automatically present in court.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi view holds that describing the property at the time of claim suffices for the validity of kafalah bi al-mal and kafalah bi al-nafs, rejecting Imam Muhammad's stricter requirement.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
10 min
Kafalah bi al-Nafs in Hudud and Qisas: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Dispute on permissibility of compelling a guarantor in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on kafalah bi al-nafs in hudud and qisas, identify their proofs, and explain the practical consequence of the dispute.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prohibits kafalah in all hudud; Sahibayn allow it in qadhf and qisas.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether a defendant accused of a hadd or qisas offense can be compelled to provide a surety for his person. The disagreement centers on the nature of these punishments—whether they involve private rights—and the scope of the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd.' Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi jurists balance textual evidence with the principle of dar' (averting punishments).

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Begin by identifying the default position according to Imam Abu Hanifa: kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible in any hadd or qisas. The judge cannot compel the defendant to provide a guarantor.
This is based on the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' and the principle of dar'.
2
Identify the exception (Sahibayn)
Contrast with the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn): kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible and compulsion is allowed in two categories: hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of zina) and qisas (retaliation). They argue that these involve a private right (haqq al-ʿabd) that necessitates securing the defendant.
In pure Allah's rights like hadd zina, even voluntary kafalah is not accepted.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the evidence for each position. Abu Hanifa relies on the general hadith and the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (dar'). The Sahibayn rely on qiyas: in qadhf, the victim needs to bring witnesses and defendant; in qisas, the guardian can forgive or take compensation, so the defendant can be compelled like in other private rights.
The Sahibayn distinguish between pure Allah's rights and mixed rights.
4
Explain the practical difference
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: In a qadhf case, under Abu Hanifa the defendant cannot be forced to provide a surety; under Sahibayn he can be compelled. In qisas, similarly, the killer can be forced to provide a surety according to Sahibayn, but not according to Abu Hanifa.
This affects whether the defendant may be imprisoned or released pending trial.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's view, as the hadith is general and the principle of dar' applies to all hudud. The author of al-Hidayah and later Hanafi scholars maintain this preference.
Even though the Sahibayn's view is recorded, the mufta bihi is the stricter position.

حدود و قصاص میں کفالت بالنفس جائز نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
قال: ولا يجوز الكفالة بالنفس فى الحدود والقصاص عند ابي حنيفة معناه لا يجبر عليها عنده وقالا يجبر في حد القذف لان فيه حق العبدو فى القصاص لانه خالص حق العبد بخلاف الحدود الخالصة لله تعالى ولابي حنيفة قوله عليه السلام لا كفالة في حدّ من غير فصل ولان مبنى الكل على الدرء فلا يجب فيها الاستيثاق لاف سائر الحقوق لانها لا تندرئ بالشبهات فيليق بها الاستيثاق كما في التعزير
ترجمہ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک حدود و قصاص میں کفالہ بالنفس جائز نہیں ہے اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ( جس پر حد یا قصاص کا دعوی کیا گیا ) اس کو کفالہ پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ حد قذف میں (کفیل دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اسلئے کہ حد قذف میں بندے کا حق ہے اور قصاص میں (بھی کفیل دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا) کیونکہ وہ خالص بندے کا حق ہے برخلاف ان حدود کے جو خالص اللہ کا حق ہے۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بغیر تفصیل کے فرمایا ہے کہ کسی حد میں کفالت نہیں ہے اور اسلئے کہ تمام حدود کی بنا ، چونکہ ساقط کرنے پر ہے اسلئے حدود میں مضبوطی کرنا بھی واجب نہ ہوگا۔ برخلاف دوسرے حقوق کے کیونکہ وہ شبہات کی وجہ سے ساقط نہیں ہوتے۔ لہذا ان کو مضبوط بنانا مناسب ہے۔ جیسے تعزیر میں ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک حدود اور قصاص میں کفالہ بالنفس جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس عبارت سے صاحب قدوری کی مراد یہ ہے کہ جس شخص پر حد یا قصاص کا دعوی کیا گیا اگر اس سے مدعی نے کفیل بنفسہ کا مطالبہ کیا یعنی ایک ایسے کفیل کا مطالبہ کیا جو اس پر حد ثابت کرانے کیلئے اس کو مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنے کا ضامن ہومگر اس نے کفیل دینے سے انکار کر دیا تو امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک اسکوفیل دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائیگا۔ پس لا تجوز الكفالة بالنفس کے معنی ہوں گے لا یجوزا جبار الكفالة یعنی جس پر حد یا قصاص واجب ہے اس کو فیل دینے پر مجبور کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ یہی امام احمد کا قول ہے اور ایک قول امام شافعی کا ہے۔ صاحبین نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس شخص پر حد قذف کا دعوی کیا گیا ہے اس کو کفیل دینے پر مجبورکیا جائیگا۔ یعنی شخص اگر کفیل دینے سے انکار کر دے تو اس کو نہیں بنفسہ دینے پر مجبور کرنا جائز ہے۔ یہی امام مالک کا قول ہے اور امام شافعی کا ایک قول بھی یہی ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حد قذف میں اپنے اوپر سے عار دور کرنے کیلئے مقذوف یعنی بندے کا حق ہے اور چونکہ حد مشروع کرنے سے مقصودلوگوں کو تہمت سے روکنا اور عالم کو فساد سے خالی کرنا ہے اسلئے حد قذف اللہ تعالیٰ کا بھی حق ہے۔ بہر حال حد قذف میں بندے کا حق ثابت ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ حد قذف جاری کرنے کیلئے مقذوف کا دعوی کرنا شرط ہے۔ اگر حد قذف مقذوف یعنی اس آدمی کا حق نہ ہوتا جس پر تہمت لگائی گئی ہے تو حد قذف جاری کرنے کیلئے اس کا دعوی کرنا شرط نہ ہوگا۔ پس دعوی کا شرط ہونا اس بات کی علامت ہے کہ حد قذف ، بندے یعنی مقذوف کا حق ہے اور مدعی یعنی مقذوف بھی اس بات کا محتاج ہوتا ہے کہ وہ اپنے گواہوں اور مدعی علیہ یعنی قاذف کو جمع کرے۔ مگر مدعی علیہ یعنی قاذف اپنے آپ کو چھپاتا ہے تو ایسی صورت میں مدعی علیہ یعنی قاذف سے نفیل بنفسہ لینے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے۔ جو قاذف کو مجلس قاضی میں حاضر کرنے کا ضامن ہو۔ پس اس ضرورت کے پیش نظر مدعی یعنی مقذوف کے دفع عار کے حق کو ثابت کرنے کیلئے قاذف کو کفیل بنفسہ دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ جیسا کہ دوسرے حقوق میں مدعی علیہ کو نفیل بنفسہ دینے پر مجبور کیا جاتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ قصاص میں بھی قاتل کو کفیل بالنفس دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا اور صاحب ہدایہ نے دلیل میں فرمایا کہ قصاص خالص بندہ کا حق ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ صحیح بات یہ ہے کہ قصاص میں بندہ کا حق بھی موجود ہے اور اللہ کا حق بھی موجود ہے البتہ بندہ کا حق غالب ہے۔ قصاص بندہ کا حق تو اسلئے ہے کہ بندہ یعنی مقتول کا ولی اگر قصاص کو معاف کرنا چاہے تو معاف کر سکتا ہے اور اگر وہ قاتل سے قصاص کا عوض لینا چاہے تو عوض بھی لے سکتا ہے۔ پس بندے یعنی ولی مقتول کو قصاص معاف کر دینے اور عوض لینے کا حق حاصل ہونا اس بات کی دلیل ہے کہ قصاص اس کا حق ہے اور اللہ کا حق اسلئے ہے کہ قصاص کی وجہ سے عالم کو فساد سے نجات ملتی ہے۔ چنانچہ قرآن پاک اعلان کرتا ہے ولکم فی القصاص حیواۃ اور عالم کو فساد سے نجات دلانا ظاہر ہے۔ یہ اللہ کا حق ہو سکتا ہے بندے کا حق نہیں ہو سکتا۔ بہر حال قصاص میں چونکہ بندے کا حق غالب ہے اور حقوق العباد ثابت کرنے کیلئے مدعی علیہ کو فیل بانفس دینے پر مجبور کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ اسلئے قصاص میں بھی قاتل کو فیل بالنفس دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ اس کے برخلاف وہ حدود جو خالص اللہ کا حق ہیں جیسے حد زنا اور حد شرب خمر کہ جس پر حد زنا یا حد شرب خمر واجب ہو اس کو نفیل بانس دینے پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائیگا۔ اگر چہ مدعی علیہ یعنی حس پر حد زنا یا حد شرب خمر واجب ہے وہ خوشدلی کے ساتھ کفیل دینا چاہے تب بھی کفیل نہیں لیا جائے گا۔ حد زنا اور حد شرب خمر میں کفیل با نفس نہ تو زنا اور شرب خمر پر شہادت قائم ہونے کے بعد لیا جائے گا اور نہ شہادت قائم ہونے سے پہلے ۔ شہادت قائم ہونے سے پہلے تو اسلئے کہ شہادت قائم ہونے سے پہلے محض دعویٰ کی وجہ سے مدعی علیہ پر مجلس قاضی میں حاضر ہونا واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ بغیر شہادت کے زنا اور شرب خمر میں کسی کا دعوئی قابل سماعت نہیں ہوتا ۔ پس جب اصیل یعنی مدعی علیہ پر مجلس قاضی میں حاضر ہونا واجب نہیں ہے تو کفیل پر اس کو حاضر کرنا کیسے واجب ہوگا۔ اور جب کفیل پر مدعی علیہ کو حاضر کرنا واجب نہیں ہو سکتا تو کفالہ با نفس کس طرح جائز ہوگا۔ اور شہادت قائم ہونے کے بعد کفالہ با نفس اسلئے جائز نہیں کہ شہادت کے بعد اور گواہوں کی تعدیل سے پہلے مدعی علیہ (جس پر زنا ، شرب خمر کا دعویٰ کیا گیا ہے ) کو قید کر لیا جاتا ہے اور قید کرنے سے مضبوطی اور وثیقہ حاصل ہو جاتا ہے یعنی قید کرنے سے مدعی علیہ کے اپنے آپ کو چھپانے اور مجلس قاضی میں حاضر نہ ہونے کا احتمال جاتا رہا اور جب یہ احتمال نہ رہا تو کفالہ کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ کفالہ بالنفس کا مقصد یہی ہے کہ کفیل مدعی علیہ کو جلس قاضی میں پیش کر دے اور یہ مقصد چونکہ بغیر کفالہ کے حاصل ہو گیا۔ اس لئے کفالہ کی کوئی ضرورت بھی نہ ہوگی ۔ اور جب اس صورت میں کنالہ بلا ضرورت رہا تو کفالہ جائز بھی نہ ہوگا۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل لا كفالة في حد حدیث ہے یعنی کسی حد میں کفالہ نہیں ہے اور یہ حدیث مطلق ہے نہ اس میں ان حدود کا ذکر ہے جو خالص اللہ کا حق ہیں اور نہ ان حدود کا ذکر ہے جن میں بندوں کا حق ہوتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ حدود میں بلاتفصیل کفالہ
Kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible in hudud and qisas, statements of the jurists. He said: Kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible in hudud and qisas according to Abu Hanifa, meaning he does not compel it. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is compelled in hadd al-qadhf because there is a right of the servant, and in qisas because it is a pure right of the servant, unlike the hudud that are purely the right of Allah. And Abu Hanifa's proof is his (peace be upon him) saying: 'No kafalah in any hadd' without distinction, and because the foundation of all (hudud) is on aversion (dar'), so securing (istithaq) is not obligatory in them, unlike other rights because they are not averted by doubts, so securing is appropriate for them as in ta'zir.
Translation: And according to Imam Abu Hanifa, kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible in hudud and qisas, meaning that the one against whom a hadd or qisas claim is made cannot be compelled to provide a guarantor. And the Sahibayn said: In hadd al-qadhf, he is compelled to provide a guarantor because hadd al-qadhf contains a right of the servant, and in qisas he is also compelled because it is a pure right of the servant, unlike the hudud that are purely the right of Allah. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said without distinction: 'There is no kafalah in any hadd,' and because the foundation of all hudud is on aversion (dar'), so securing is not obligatory in them, unlike other rights because they are not averted by doubts, so securing is appropriate for them, as in ta'zir. Explanation: Sahib al-Quduri says that according to Imam Abu Hanifa, kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible in hudud and qisas. By this phrase, Sahib al-Quduri means that if the claimant demands a guarantor from the one against whom a hadd or qisas claim is made—i.e., a guarantor who would guarantee to bring him to the judge's court to establish the hadd—and he refuses to provide a guarantor, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa he will not be compelled to provide a guarantor. Thus, 'la tajuz al-kafalah bi al-nafs' means 'la yajuz ijbar al-kafalah,' i.e., it is not permissible to compel the one upon whom hadd or qisas is obligatory to provide a guarantor. This is also the saying of Imam Ahmad and one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. The Sahibayn said that the one against whom hadd al-qadhf is claimed is compelled to provide a guarantor; that is, if the person refuses to provide a guarantor, it is permissible to compel him to provide a guarantor for the person. This is also the saying of Imam Malik and one saying of Imam al-Shafi'i. The Sahibayn's proof is that hadd al-qadhf contains a right of the servant (the victim of slander) to remove disgrace from himself, and since the purpose of legislation of the hadd is to prevent people from slander and to purify the world from corruption, hadd al-qadhf is also a right of Allah. Nevertheless, in hadd al-qadhf, a right of the servant is established. For this reason, for executing hadd al-qadhf, the claim of the victim is a condition. If hadd al-qadhf were not a right of the person who was slandered, then his claim would not be a condition for executing it. Thus, the conditionality of the claim is an indication that hadd al-qadhf is a right of the servant (the victim). And the claimant (the victim) needs to gather his witnesses and the defendant (the slanderer). But if the defendant hides himself, then in such a case, the need arises to take a guarantor for the person from the defendant, who would guarantee to bring the defendant to the judge's court. So, in view of this need, to establish the right of the victim to remove disgrace, the slanderer is compelled to provide a guarantor for his person, just as in other rights the defendant is compelled to provide a guarantor for person. The Sahibayn say that in qisas as well, the killer is compelled to provide a guarantor for his person. And the author of al-Hidayah said as proof that qisas is a pure right of the servant, but it is not like that. Rather, the correct view is that in qisas, there is a right of the servant and also a right of Allah; however, the right of the servant predominates. It is a right of the servant because the guardian of the slain can forgive qisas or can take compensation from the killer. So the guardian's right to forgive or take compensation is evidence that qisas is his right. And it is Allah's right because through qisas, the world is saved from corruption. Indeed, the Holy Quran declares: 'And there is life for you in qisas.' Saving the world from corruption is obviously a right of Allah, not a right of the servant. Nevertheless, since the right of the servant predominates in qisas, and for establishing rights of servants, the defendant can be compelled to provide a guarantor for the person, therefore in qisas too, the killer is compelled to provide a guarantor for the person. Contrary to hudud that are purely Allah's right, such as hadd of zina and hadd of drinking alcohol: the one upon whom hadd zina or hadd shurb khamr is obligatory is not compelled to provide a guarantor for his person. Even if the defendant (against whom zina or drinking is claimed) willingly wants to provide a guarantor, it will not be accepted. In hadd zina and hadd shurb khamr, a guarantor for the person is not taken, neither after testimony is established nor before. Before testimony, because before testimony, merely by virtue of a claim, it is not obligatory upon the defendant to appear in the judge's court. Since without testimony, a claim in zina and drinking is not admissible. So when it is not obligatory upon the original (defendant) to appear in the judge's court, how can it be obligatory upon the guarantor to produce him? And when it cannot be obligatory upon the guarantor to produce the defendant, how can kafalah bi al-nafs be permissible? And after testimony, kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible because after testimony and before validation of witnesses, the defendant (against whom zina or drinking is claimed) is imprisoned, and imprisonment provides security and surety; i.e., imprisonment removes the likelihood of the defendant hiding or not appearing in court. When this likelihood is removed, there is no need for kafalah. Because the purpose of kafalah bi al-nafs is that the guarantor produces the defendant in court, and since this purpose is achieved without kafalah, there is no need for kafalah. And when in this situation kafalah is without need, it is not permissible. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' – i.e., there is no kafalah in any hadd. And this hadith is absolute (general); it does not mention hudud that are purely Allah's right nor hudud that involve rights of servants. Thus it is understood that in hudud, without distinction, kafalah
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the permissibility of compelling a defendant to provide a surety (kafalah bi al-nafs) in cases of hudud (prescribed punishments) and qisas (retaliation). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that such compulsion is not allowed in any hadd or qisas, based on the general hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' (No suretyship in any prescribed punishment) and the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (dar'), so securing the defendant is not necessary. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) distinguish: in hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of adultery) and qisas, where a private right (haqq al-‘abd) predominates, compulsion is allowed. In pure Allah's rights like hadd zina and shurb khamr, even voluntary kafalah is not accepted because imprisonment provides sufficient security. The text explains the reasoning: in hadd al-qadhf, the victim needs to produce witnesses and the defendant; if the defendant hides, a surety is necessary. In qisas, the victim's guardian has the right to forgive or take compensation, so the defendant can be compelled. The commentary (tashrih) clarifies that Abu Hanifa's ruling means the judge cannot force a surety, but a voluntary contract is also considered invalid in hudud and qisas according to Abu Hanifa. The discussion includes references to opinions of Imam Ahmad, Imam Shafi‘i, and Imam Malik.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): Suretyship for the person, where the guarantor undertakes to produce the principal (the debtor/defendant) in court.
حد (hadd): A fixed punishment prescribed by Islamic law for specific offenses (e.g., zina, qadhf, shurb khamr).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for homicide or bodily harm, where the victim's guardian can demand execution, forgive, or take compensation.
درء (dar'): The principle of averting hudud by doubts; punishments are to be avoided in case of uncertainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, why is kafalah bi al-nafs not allowed in hudud?
A) Because hudud are based on the principle of dar' (averting by doubts), so securing the defendant is unnecessary.
B) Because hudud involve only the rights of Allah, so no private claims exist.
C) Because the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' is general and includes all hudud.
D) All of the above.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's prohibition of kafalah in all hudud and qisas is the relied-upon position, supported by the general hadith and the principle of dar'.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
12 min
Compelling Kafalah bi al-Nafs in Hadd and Qisas
Explains when a defendant can be compelled to provide a surety in hudud and qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compelling a defendant to provide kafalah bi al-nafs in hudud and qisas, and distinguish between cases where compulsion is wajib and where it is not based on the nature of the right.

Core Idea
Compulsion for kafalah bi al-nafs is wajib only when the servant's right is predominant over Allah's right.

In this passage, the commentator on al-Hidayah explores whether a defendant can be compelled to provide a surety for his person (kafalah bi al-nafs) in different types of hadd and qisas cases. The key is whether the right involved is purely Allah's right, a pure servant's right, or a mixed right where the servant's right dominates. This leads to a notable intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding qisas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core distinction
Recognize that the ruling on compelling kafalah bi al-nafs hinges on the nature of the right: haqq Allah (pure Allah's right) vs. haqq al-'abd (servant's right) vs. a mix where one dominates.
2
Examine hadd al-qadhf as a model
The text uses hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of adultery) as a paradigm of a servant's right, where compulsion is allowed because the claimant needs to bring the defendant to court to clear his name.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position on qisas
The Sahibayn extend compulsion to qisas, arguing that it is predominantly a servant's right. The text clarifies that qisas is mixed but the servant's right is predominant, justifying compulsion.
4
Contrast with pure hudud
For pure Allah's rights (like hadd al-zina and hadd al-shurb), compulsion is not allowed, and even voluntary kafalah is invalid due to the nature of hudud being built on dropping (isqat) and the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd'.
5
Understand the tarjih within the Hanafi school
The commentator prefers the Sahibayn's view on qisas as mufta bihi, despite Abu Hanifa's objection based on the hadith and the principle of isqat. Identify the reasoning and authority used.

Book of Kafalah. The right does not belong to the one accused; to execute the hadd of qadhf, his claim is not a condition. So the condition of a claim is a sign that the hadd of qadhf is a right of the servant, i.e., the one accused of qadhf (maqdhuuf), and the claimant (maqdhuuf) also needs to gather his witnesses and the defendant (qaadhif). But if the defendant hides, then the need arises to take a surety for the person (nafil binnafs) from the defendant, i.e., one who guarantees to present the qaadhif in the judge's court. Therefore, due to this need, to establish the right of the claimant to remove the disgrace, the qaadhif will be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs, just as in other rights the defendant is compelled to provide a nafil binnafs. The Sahibayn say that in qisas as well, the killer will be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs, and the author of al-Hidayah argued that qisas is a pure right of the servant, but this is not so. Rather, the correct view is that in qisas there is both a right of the servant and a right of Allah, but the servant's right is predominant. Qisas is a right of the servant because the heir of the slain can forgive qisas or take compensation. That he has the right to forgive or take compensation indicates it is his right. And it is a right of Allah because through qisas the world is saved from corruption, as the Qur'an says: 'And in qisas there is life for you.' Saving the world from corruption is clearly a right of Allah, not of the servant. In any case, since the servant's right is predominant in qisas, and to establish rights of the servant the defendant can be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs, therefore in qisas the killer will be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs. In contrast, those hudud that are purely the right of Allah, like the hadd of zina and the hadd of drinking khamr, the person upon whom such hadd is wajib will not be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs. Even if he willingly offers a kafil, it will not be accepted. In the hadd of zina and hadd of drinking khamr, a kafil binnafs will be taken neither after the establishment of testimony nor before. Before testimony because merely a claim does not make it wajib for the defendant to appear in court, since without testimony a claim in zina and khamr is not admissible. So when the principal (defendant) is not obliged to appear, how can the kafil be obliged to bring him? And when the kafil cannot be obliged, kafalah binnafs cannot be valid. After testimony, kafalah binnafs is not valid because after testimony and before evaluation of witnesses, the defendant is imprisoned, and imprisonment provides strength and security; the possibility of his hiding or not attending disappears, so there is no need for kafalah. Since the purpose of kafalah binnafs is for the kafil to present the defendant, and that purpose is achieved without kafalah, there is no need, and thus it is not valid. The proof of Imam Abu Hanifa is the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' (no kafalah in hadd). This hadith is absolute; it does not specify hudud that are purely Allah's right nor those with a servant's right. So it indicates that in all hudud without distinction, there is no kafalah, whether hadd qadhf, qisas, or hudud that are purely Allah's. Regarding this hadith, al-Khassaf's opinion is that it is the saying of Shuraih, not of the Prophet (peace be upon him). But Sadr al-Shahid has raised it to the Prophet (peace be upon him). The second proof is that all hudud are based on dropping (saqit). The rule of hudud is that they are dropped due to doubts (shubuhat). To strengthen something that is prone to be dropped by taking a kafil cannot be wajib. So it is established that in hudud, strengthening via kafalah is not wajib. In contrast, other rights are not subject to being dropped by doubts, so strengthening them via kafalah is appropriate, as in ta'zir. In ta'zir, the person upon whom ta'zir is wajib will be compelled to provide a kafil binnafs, because ta'zir is only the right of the servant; it is dropped by forgiveness, and doubts do not affect it. So like financial rights, in ta'zir the defendant will be compelled to provide a kafil.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah deals with the ruling on compelling a defendant to provide a surety for his person (kafalah bi al-nafs) in various types of hudud and qisas. The discussion hinges on the nature of the right involved: whether it is a pure right of Allah, a pure right of the servant, or a mixed right. The author begins with hadd al-qadhf (false accusation of adultery), which is a right of the servant (the accused). Since the plaintiff (the accused) needs to bring the defendant to court to establish the hadd and clear his name, and the defendant may hide, the court compels the defendant to provide a kafil who guarantees his appearance. This is similar to other rights of servants. Then the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) extend compulsion to qisas, arguing that qisas is a right of the servant. The text corrects this by noting that qisas is mixed: the heir can forgive or take compensation (servant's right), but it also preserves societal order (Allah's right). However, since the servant's right is predominant, compulsion is allowed. This is the position of the Sahibayn and supported by the commentator. In contrast, hudud that are purely Allah's right, such as hadd al-zina and hadd al-shurb al-khamr, compulsion is not allowed, and even voluntary kafalah is invalid. The text provides two proofs: (1) the hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' which Imam Abu Hanifa uses to deny all kafalah in hudud, though the commentator notes it may not be authentic; (2) hudud are built on dropping (isqat) due to doubts, so strengthening them via kafalah is inconsistent. Finally, ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is treated as a pure right of the servant, so compulsion is allowed like financial rights. Overall, the passage clarifies that the permissibility of compulsion for kafalah bi al-nafs depends on the predominance of the servant's right in the claim.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): A contract where a surety guarantees to present the principal (defendant) in court.
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right belonging to Allah that is not subject to private waiver.
حق العبد (haqq al-'abd): A right belonging to the human being that can be forgiven or compromised.
حد (hadd): A fixed corporeal punishment prescribed by Shariah for major sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (Sahibayn), in which type of claim is a defendant compelled to provide kafalah bi al-nafs?
A) Hadd al-zina (adultery)
B) Hadd al-shurb al-khamr (drinking wine)
C) Qisas (retaliation)
D) All hudud equally

Key Takeaway
Compulsion for kafalah bi al-nafs is permitted only where the servant's right is predominant, as in qisas and hadd al-qadhf, but prohibited in pure Allah's rights like zina and shurb al-khamr.

Kafalah — Surety

Voluntary Kafalah bi al-Nafs in Hudud and Qisas
Ruling on voluntary kafalah in hudud and qisas when the defendant willingly offers a surety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on voluntary kafalah bi al-nafs in hadd al-qadhf and qisas, explain the reasoning based on ijma and the wajib nature of taslim al-nafs, and identify the exception for pure Allah's hudud.

Core Idea
Voluntary kafalah bi al-nafs in hadd al-qadhf and qisas is valid by consensus because the defendant's obligation to surrender himself makes the kafil's duty feasible.

This passage clarifies that while compulsory kafalah in hudud is disputed between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, voluntary kafalah in hadd al-qadhf and qisas is unanimously valid. The key principle is that the defendant's wajib duty to appear in court (taslim al-nafs) allows the kafil's obligation to be attached, achieving damm al-dhimmah. However, this ruling does not apply to pure Allah's hudud like zina or drinking wine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (sahih, fasid, etc.)? The text states that voluntary kafalah bi al-nafs in hadd al-qadhf and qisas is 'sahih' by consensus.
The ruling is based on ijma, making it qat'i.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The text explicitly states 'بالاجماع' (by consensus). Identify the type of dalil (Ijma) and its epistemological weight.
Ijma is a primary source; its ruling is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the ruling? The reasoning is that in these hudud, the defendant's taslim al-nafs is wajib. Therefore, the kafil can be demanded to bring him to court, realizing the essence of kafalah: damm al-dhimmah ila al-dhimmah in demand.
The feasibility of the kafil's obligation depends on the defendant's own obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement? The passage mentions a dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn about compulsion, but not about voluntary kafalah. Thus, voluntary kafalah is uncontested.
The ikhtilaf is only about whether the judge can compel the defendant to give a kafil.
5
Identify the exception
Where does the ruling NOT apply? The passage explicitly excludes pure Allah's hudud (e.g., hadd al-zina, hadd al-shurb al-khamr). In these, even voluntary kafalah is invalid.
This distinction is based on the nature of the right: mixed (huquq al-ibad) vs. pure Allah's rights.

And if his soul makes him generous (i.e., the defendant willingly offers), it is valid by consensus, because it is possible to impose its obligation (muijib) upon the contract. Because handing over the person (taslim al-nafs) in these (hudud) is wajib for the defendant, so the kafil can also be demanded to bring him, thus the meaning of adjunction (damm) is realized. Urdu translation: And if the defendant's heart chooses to give a kafil himself, then kafalah is valid by consensus. Because it is possible to attach its obligation to the contract of kafalah. Because in hudud, the defendant's handing over of himself is wajib. Since he can be demanded from the kafil as well, the meaning of adjunction is realized. Explanation: The issue is that in those hudud (like hadd al-qadhf) and qisas, there is a dispute between Imam (Abu Hanifa) and the Sahibayn regarding compulsion. In these, if the defendant willingly provides a kafil without compulsion, this kafalah is valid by consensus. The proof is that the obligation of kafalah can be attached to the contract. That is, the obligation of kafalah is to present the defendant in court, and in hadd al-qadhf and qisas, it is wajib upon the defendant to present himself. So when the defendant is required to attend, the kafil can also be demanded to bring him, and since both the defendant and the kafil can be demanded, the meaning of kafalah (joining of liability in demand) is realized. Thus, kafalah becomes valid. Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage addresses voluntary kafalah bi al-nafs in hudud and qisas. It begins by stating that if a defendant in a hadd or qisas case willingly offers a surety (without compulsion), the kafalah is valid by consensus (ijma'). The reason given is that the obligation of kafalah (the kafil's duty to bring the defendant) can be attached to the contract, because the defendant himself is obliged to appear in court. Thus, the kafil's duty is an extension of that obligation, and the merging of liabilities (damm al-dhimmah ila al-dhimmah) is achieved. The commentary clarifies that this applies to hudud like hadd al-qadhf and qisas, where there is ikhtilaf about compulsion. However, voluntary kafalah is unanimously valid. The text then reiterates that in hudud that are purely the right of Allah (e.g., zina, shurb al-khamr), even voluntary kafalah is invalid, as previously stated. The ruling is based on the feasibility of the kafil's obligation being derived from the defendant's obligation. The use of 'ijma'' indicates the consensus of the scholars on this point, at least within the Hanafi school or more broadly.

Key Terms
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the scholars, used here to establish the validity of voluntary kafalah.
تسليم النفس (taslim al-nafs): The defendant's duty to surrender himself or appear in court.
ضم الذمة إلى الذمة (damm al-dhimmah ila al-dhimmah): The merger of liabilities, meaning the kafil's liability is added to the principal's liability in terms of demand.

Key Takeaway
Voluntary kafalah bi al-nafs in hadd al-qadhf and qisas is valid by consensus, while it remains invalid in pure Allah's hudud.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
6 min
Voluntary Kafalah in Hudud and Qisas
Ruling with proof on voluntary kafalah in hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling and scope of voluntary kafalah in hudud and qisas, and identify which types of hudud allow it by consensus.

Core Idea
Voluntary kafalah in hudud is valid only when the hadd involves a personal right, not pure divine rights.

Kafalah (suretyship for the person) is generally a permissible contract, but its application in hudud requires careful distinction. This lesson examines a specific ruling: when the defendant willingly provides a surety in cases of qadhf (false accusation of zina) and qisas (retaliation), the kafalah is valid by consensus. The proof relies on the fact that the defendant is already obliged to present himself, so the surety can be required to do the same. However, this does not apply to hudud that are purely Allah's rights, such as hadd zina or drinking wine.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what legal act is being ruled upon and its hukm level. Here, the act is kafalah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person) in hudud and qisas, provided voluntarily. The ruling is ja'iz (permissible, mubah) by consensus.
2
Analyze the condition for validity
The key condition is that the surety must be provided voluntarily by the defendant without compulsion. Also, the hadd must involve a personal right (haqq al-'abd) such as qadhf and qisas, not a pure divine right (haqq Allah).
Compulsion is a separate dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn; here we focus on voluntary.
3
Understand the dalil (proof)
The proof is a qiyas: since the defendant is obliged to present himself in court for qadhf and qisas, the surety can also be obliged to present him. This realizes the essence of kafalah: joining of responsibility (ضم الذمة إلى الذمة).
The text explicitly says: 'because it is possible to apply the effect of kafalah to the contract... surrendering the person is wajib.'
4
Distinguish between types of hudud
Not all hudud are alike. Hudud that are purely Allah's right (e.g., zina, drinking) are not subject to kafalah even voluntarily, because they are meant to be dropped by doubts and lack inherent strength. Kafalah would be inappropriate.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.

كتاب الكفاله

اشرف البدایہ جلد نم نہیں ہے خواہ حد قذف ہو یا قصاص ہو یا حدود خالصہ اللہ ہوں۔ اس حدیث کے بارے میں خصاف کی رائے یہ ہے کہ یہ حضرت شریح کا کلام ہے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا کلام نہیں ہے۔ لیکن صدر الشہید نے اس حدیث کو رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم تک مرفوع کیا ہے۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ تمام حدود کی بنا ساقط کرنے پر ہے۔ تمام حدود کا حکم یہ ہے کہ ان کو شہات کی وجہ سے ساقط کر دیا جائے اور جن چیزوں کی بنیاد ساقط کرنے پر ہو۔ ان کو نفیل لے کر مضبوط کرنا کیسے واجب ہو گا یعنی جو حق شبہ سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہو اس میں بذات خود مضبوطی نہیں ہے اور جس حق میں بذات خود مضبوطی نہ ہو اس میں کفالہ سے مضبوطی پیدا کرتا کس طرح لازم ہو سکتا ہے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ حدود میں کفالہ کے ذریعہ مضبوطی پیدا کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ اسکے برخلاف دوسرے حقوق کہ وہ شبہات کی وجہ سے ساتھ نہیں ہوتے۔ لہذا کفالہ کے ذریعہ ان کو مضبوط کرنا مناسب ہے۔ جیسے تعزیر میں ہے۔ یعنی جس چیز میں تعزیر واجب ہو اس میں من وجب عليه التعزیر کو لفیل بالنفس دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ تعزیر فقط ہندہ کا حق ہے۔ اس کے ساقط کرنے سے ساقط ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور شبہات کے ساتھ ثابت ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس مالی حقوق کی طرح تعزیر میں بھی مدعی علیہ کو فیل دینے پر مجبور کیا جائے گا۔
مدعی علیہ کا دل خود کفیل دینے پر ایثار کرے کفالت بالا جماع جائز ہے
ولو سمحت نفسه به يصح بالاجماع لانه امکن ترتیب موجبه عليه لان تسليم النفس فيها واجب فيطاله به الكفيل فيتحقق الضم

یہ خیال رہے کہ وہ حدود جو خالصتہ اللہ کاحق ہیں جیسے حد نا اور حد شرب خمران میں اگرخود مدعی علیہ بھی بغیر جبر کے اپنی خوشدلی سے کفیل پیش کرے تب بھی کفالہ جائز نہیں ہے جیسا کہ گذشتہ مسئلہ میں بیان کیا جا چکا ہے۔
Book of Kafalah. 150. Ashraf al-Bidaya, volume number does not exist, whether it is hadd qadhf or qisas or hadd purely for Allah. Regarding this hadith, Khasaf's opinion is that it is the speech of Hadrat Shuraih, not the speech of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). But Sadr al-Shahid has raised this hadith as marfu' to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him). The second evidence is that all hudud are based on dropping. The ruling of all hudud is that they are dropped due to doubts. And things that are based on dropping, how can they be strengthened by taking a surety? That is, a right that is dropped due to doubt has no inherent strength. And a right that has no inherent strength, how can it be necessary to strengthen it through kafalah? So it became known that in hudud, it is not obligatory to strengthen through kafalah. Contrary to other rights, they are not subject to doubts. Therefore, strengthening them through kafalah is appropriate, like in ta'zir. That is, something in which ta'zir is obligatory, the one upon whom ta'zir is obligatory will be compelled to give a surety of the person, because ta'zir is only the right of the individual. It is dropped by dropping, and is established with doubts. So like financial rights, in ta'zir the defendant will be compelled to give a surety. If the defendant's heart inclines to give a surety himself, then kafalah is valid by consensus. Translation: And if the defendant's heart inclines to give a surety himself, then kafalah is valid by consensus, because it is possible to apply the effect of kafalah to the contract of kafalah, because surrendering the person in these is obligatory, so the surety can demand it from him, and thus the meaning of inclusion is realized. Explanation: The issue is that there is a difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether the defendant is compelled to give a surety in hudud (hadd qadhf) and qisas. If the defendant willingly provides a surety without compulsion, then this kafalah is valid by consensus. The evidence is that it is possible to apply the effect of kafalah to the contract of kafalah. In this manner, the effect of kafalah is the presentation of the defendant's person in the court of the judge, and it is obligatory upon the defendant in both hadd qadhf and qisas to present himself in the court. So since the presence is obligatory upon the defendant, the surety can also be demanded to present him. And when the surety can be demanded to present the defendant, and also the defendant himself can be demanded to present himself, then the meaning of kafalah, which is the joining of the responsibility to the responsibility in demand, is realized. And when the meaning of kafalah is realized, this kafalah will be valid. It should be kept in mind that in hudud that are purely the right of Allah, such as hadd zina and hadd drinking wine, even if the defendant himself willingly provides a surety without compulsion, even then kafalah is not valid, as has been stated in the previous issue.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the validity of kafalah (suretyship) in hudud and qisas when provided voluntarily. The author, Ashraf al-Hidaya, explains that there is a dispute regarding the hadith that says the Prophet ﷺ did not accept surety in hudud. Khasaf considers it from Shuraih, while Sadr al-Shahid considers it marfu'. The author then presents a rational argument: hudud are based on dropping due to doubts, so they lack inherent strength; thus, strengthening them through kafalah is not wajib. However, for rights not subject to doubts (like ta'zir and financial rights), kafalah strengthens them and is appropriate. When the defendant willingly offers a surety, it is valid by consensus because the effect of kafalah (presenting the defendant in court) is possible—since the defendant is already obliged to present himself in qadhf and qisas, the surety can also be held to that obligation, realizing the meaning of kafalah (ضم الذمة إلى الذمة). Crucially, this applies only to hudud that involve personal rights (qadhf, qisas). For hudud that are purely divine rights (hadd zina, hadd shurb al-khamr), kafalah is not valid even if voluntary. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether the defendant can be compelled to provide a surety in these cases, but the ruling here is on voluntary provision.

Key Terms
کفالہ (kafalah): Suretyship; a contract by which one person (kafil) guarantees the presence of another (asil) in court for a claim involving the person (nafs).
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Allah for specific crimes like zina, qadhf, theft, etc.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliatory punishment for intentional murder or bodily harm.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of hudud is voluntary kafalah (suretyship for the person) valid by consensus?
A) Hadd zina only
B) Hadd shurb al-khamr only
C) Hadd qadhf and qisas
D) All hudud without exception

Key Takeaway
Voluntary kafalah in hudud is valid by consensus only for hudud that involve a personal right, such as qadhf and qisas, because the defendant's presence is already obligatory and the surety can be held to that obligation.

Rahn and Kafalah in Kharaj: Permissibility Based on Debt Character
Ruling statement with expansion on permissibility of rahn and kafalah in kharaj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rahn and kafalah in kharaj and explain why the debt character of kharaj makes them permissible.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a demandable debt, so rahn and kafalah—normally for debts—are permissible for it.

This passage from al-Quduri's matn, elaborated by later commentators, establishes a key principle: financial obligations like kharaj (land tax) follow the same rules as ordinary debts in contracts of rahn and kafalah. Understanding this analogy is essential to see how Hanafi fiqh treats state fiscal claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the explicit ruling: both rahn and kafalah are jā'iz (permissible) in the context of kharaj.
The ruling is from the Quduri matn and is affirmed in Hidayah.
2
Pinpoint the legal cause (illah)
The text gives the reason: 'because it (kharaj) is a debt that is demanded and possible to collect.'
This illah connects kharaj to ordinary debts.
3
Trace the analogy
Recognize that kafalah is permissible for any demandable debt, and rahn is permissible as security for any collectible debt.
The commentator elaborates by noting that non-payment of kharaj leads to imprisonment and pursuit, just like any other debt.
4
Examine the textual expansion
The commentator explains that kharaj is analogous to ordinary debts in terms of enforceability, which justifies the permissibility of these contracts.
This is a hallmark of Hanafi talil (reasoning).
5
Note the linguistic structure
The phrase uses laf wa nashr ghayr murattab: 'demanded' (matlub bihi) is paired with kafalah, and 'collectible' (mumkin al-istifa) with rahn.
This non-ordered pairing is a rhetorical figure that clarifies the textual linkage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والرهن والكفالة جائزان فى الخراج لانه دين مطالب به ممكن الاستيفاء فيمكن ترتيب موجب العقد عليه فيهما ترجمہ خراج میں رہن اور کفالہ دونوں جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ خراج ایک ایسا قرضہ ہے جس کا مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے ( اور ) اس کا وصول کرتا ممکن ہے پس رہن اور کفالہ دونوں میں عقد کے موجب کو اس پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے ۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ خراج میں رہن اور کفالہ دونوں جائز ہیں۔ یعنی اگر کسی ذمی پر خراج واجب ہو اور اس کی طرف سے کوئی کفیل ہو گیا تو جائز ہے اور اگر اسے خراج کے عوض کچھ رہن دیا تو بھی جائز ہے۔ کفالہ تو اسلئے جائز ہے کہ کفالہ کہتے ہیں مطالبہ دین میں ایک ذمہ کو دوسرے ذمہ کے ساتھ ملانا اور خراج بھی ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے حتی کہ خراج ادانہ کرنے کی صورت میں ذمی کو محبوس کرایا جا سکتا ہے جیسا کہ دین ادانہ کرنے کی صورت میں مدیون اور قرضدار کو محبوس کرانا جائز ہے اور جس طرح دین ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں مدیون کا پیچھا اس طرح کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ دائن اس سے جدا نہ ہو اسی طرح خراج ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ذمی کا پیچھا بھی کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ خراج ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے اور ایسا دین جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جائے اس کا کفالہ جائز ہوتا ہے لہذ اخراج کا کفالہ بھی جائز ہوگا اور رہن اسلئے جائز ہے کہ رہن، دین وصول کرنے کا وثیقہ ہے۔ یعنی رہن کی صورت میں دین وصول ہونے کا اعتماد اور بھروسہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح رہن سے چونکہ خراج وصول کرنا ممکن ہے اسلئے جس طرح دین کی صورت میں رہن جائز ہے اسی طرح خراج میں رہن رکھنا بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس بات کو مختصر ایوں فرمایا کہ خراج چونکہ ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے اور رہن سے اس کا وصول کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اسلئے کفالہ اور رہن میں عقد کفالہ اور عقد رہن کے موجب کو خراج پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے اور جب کفالہ اور رہن میں ان کے موجب کو خراج پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے تو خراج میں کفالہ اور رہن دونوں جائز ہوں گے۔ فوائد عبارت میں چونکہ دین مطالب بہ کا تعلق کفالہ کے ساتھ ہے اور ممکن الاستیفاء کا تعلق رہن کے ساتھ ہے۔ اسلئے عبارت میں لف ونشر غیر مرتب ہوگا۔
He said: Rahn (pledge) and kafalah (suretyship) are both permissible in kharaj (land tax) because it is a debt that is demanded (matlub bihi) and possible to collect (mumkin al-istifa'), so the effect of the contract can be arranged upon it in both. Translation: Rahn and kafalah are both permissible in kharaj. Because kharaj is a debt that is demanded and its collection is possible. So in both rahn and kafalah, the effect of the contract can be arranged upon it. Explanation: Author of Quduri says that rahn and kafalah are both permissible in kharaj. That is, if a dhimmi is liable for kharaj and someone becomes a surety for him, it is permissible; and if he gives something as pledge for the kharaj, it is also permissible. Kafalah is permissible because kafalah means joining one liability to another in demanding a debt, and kharaj is a debt that is demanded from the people; even, if kharaj is not paid, the dhimmi can be imprisoned, just as a debtor can be imprisoned for non-payment of a debt. And just as in case of non-payment of debt, the debtor can be pursued such that the creditor does not separate from him, similarly for non-payment of kharaj, the dhimmi can be pursued. So it is established that kharaj is a debt that is demanded from the people, and for such a debt, kafalah is permissible. Hence kafalah for kharaj is permissible. Rahn is permissible because rahn is a security for collecting a debt; i.e., in rahn, confidence and trust in collecting the debt is achieved. So similarly, since collecting kharaj through rahn is possible, just as rahn is permissible in case of a debt, similarly giving a pledge in kharaj is permissible. The author of Hidayah has briefly stated this: because kharaj is a debt demanded from the people and its collection through rahn is possible, therefore in both kafalah and rahn, the effect of the contract of kafalah and the contract of rahn can be arranged upon kharaj. And when in kafalah and rahn, their effects can be arranged upon kharaj, then both kafalah and rahn are permissible in kharaj. Benefit: In the phrase, because 'dīn maṭlūb bihī' (debt that is demanded) is connected with kafalah, and 'mumkin al-istīfā'' (possible to collect) is connected with rahn, therefore in the phrase, there is a non-ordered intertwining (laf wa nashr ghayr murattab).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Quduri matn, expanded by the commentator. The ruling: Rahn (pledge) and kafalah (suretyship) are both permissible in the context of kharaj (land tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects). The reasoning is that kharaj is a debt that can be demanded and collected. The author explains that kafalah is permissible because it involves joining one liability to another for demanding a debt, and kharaj is such a debt—it can be demanded, and non-payment can lead to imprisonment and pursuit of the dhimmi. Therefore, kafalah is valid. Rahn is permissible because it serves as a security for the debt, and since kharaj can be collected through rahn, it is allowed. The author of Hidayah summarizes: since kharaj is a demandable debt and collection via rahn is possible, both contracts can have their effects applied to kharaj, making them permissible. A linguistic note: the phrase has 'laf wa nashr ghayr murattab' (non-ordered intertwining) where 'dīn maṭlūb bihī' refers to kafalah and 'mumkin al-istīfā'' refers to rahn, though the text places them together.

Key Terms
خراج (kharāj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmis) in an Islamic state.
دین مطالب بہ (dayn maṭlūb bihī): A debt that is legally demandable from the debtor.
لف و نشر غیر مرتب (laf wa nashr ghayr murattab): A rhetorical figure where terms are paired with their descriptors in a non-sequential order.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because kharaj is a form of charity given voluntarily.

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a demandable debt, so rahn and kafalah are permissible for it just as for any other financial obligation.

Multiple Kafils for the Same Person
Ruling on two sureties taken consecutively for the same debtor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple personal sureties and explain the reasoning based on the purpose of tawaththuq.

Core Idea
Multiple sureties for the same person are valid because each creates an independent duty to respond to demand.

This lesson examines a concise ruling from the Quduri matn on consecutive personal suretyship. The text clarifies that a second surety does not cancel the first; both remain bound. The underlying reasoning is rooted in the purpose of suretyship: to strengthen the creditor's position, which is enhanced rather than contradicted by additional sureties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The text states that if a creditor takes a kafil bil-nafs from a debtor and later takes another kafil for the same debtor, both are sureties (فهما كفيلان).
2
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The effect of kafalah is the obligation to respond to demand (التزام المطالبة). Demand can be made multiple times, so multiple sureties do not conflict.
3
Grasp the underlying principle
The purpose of suretyship is to obtain strength (التوثق). Adding a second surety increases security, so both are valid.
This principle distinguishes Hanafi law from any system that would release the first surety upon taking a second.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider: A creditor takes Ali as a surety for Zaid, then later takes Bakr as another surety for the same Zaid. Both Ali and Bakr are liable to produce Zaid upon demand.
The creditor can demand from either surety individually.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: ومن اخذ من رجل كفيلاً بنفسه ثم ذهب فاخذ منه كفيلاً آخر فهما كفيلان لان موجبه التزام المطالبة وهي متعددة والمقصود التوثق وبالثانية يزداد التوثق فلايتنافيان ترجمہ اگر کسی نے ایک آدمی سے کفیل بالنفس لیا پھر جا کر دوسرا کفیل لیا تو یہ دونوں، دوکفیل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ عقد کفالہ کا موجب زام مطالبہ ہے اور مطالبہ متعدد ہے اور عقد کفالہ کا مقصود مضبوطی حاصل کرنا ہے اور دوسرے کفالہ سے مضبوطی بڑھ جائے گی الہذا دونوں کفالتوں میں منافات نہ ہو گی۔
He said: If someone takes a surety for the person (kafil bil-nafs) from a man, then goes and takes another surety from him, then both are sureties. Because the effect of the contract (kafalah) is the obligation to demand (iltizam al-mutalaba), and demand is multiple. And the purpose is to obtain strength (tawaththuq), and by the second, strength is increased, so they do not conflict. Translation: If someone takes a surety for the person from a man, then goes and takes another surety, then both are two sureties. Because the effect of the contract of kafalah is the obligation of demand, and demand is multiple. And the purpose of the contract of kafalah is to obtain strength, and by the second kafalah, strength is increased, so there is no contradiction between the two kafalas.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement from the Quduri matn. The rule: If a creditor first takes a kafil bil-nafs (surety for the person of the debtor) and later takes another kafil bil-nafs from the same debtor for the same debt, both sureties are valid and both remain liable. The reasoning: the effect of kafalah is to obligate the surety to respond to the creditor's demand (mutalaba). Since demand can be made multiple times (the creditor can demand payment from either surety), having multiple sureties increases security. The second surety does not cancel the first; both are enforceable. This is based on the principle that the purpose of kafalah is to strengthen the creditor's position, and additional sureties only enhance that security.

Key Terms
كفيل بالنفس (kafil bil-nafs): A surety who guarantees the presence of the debtor's person (not the debt itself).
التزام المطالبة (iltizām al-muṭālaba): The obligation to respond to the creditor's demand for the debtor's presence.
توثق (tawaththuq): Strengthening or securing the creditor's position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a creditor takes a kafil bil-nafs from a debtor and later takes another kafil bil-nafs from the same debtor for the same obligation, what is the status of the first surety?
A) The first surety is released because the second replaces him.
B) Both sureties are valid and remain liable because the demand can be made multiple times.
C) Only the second surety is valid because the first contract is void.
D) The debtor must choose one surety; the other is released.

Key Takeaway
Multiple personal sureties for the same debtor are all valid and independently liable; the second does not cancel the first.

Rahn and Kafalah Permissible in Kharaj
States ruling and provides talil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rahn and kafalah in kharaj and explain the talil that kharaj is a demandable debt.

Core Idea
Kharaj is a demandable debt, so rahn and kafalah are valid like any other debt.

This lesson presents the Hanafi position that both rahn (pledge) and kafalah (suretyship) are permissible in the context of kharaj (land tax). The proof is a simple but powerful talil: kharaj is a debt that can be demanded and collected. This legal classification opens the door for all the normal debt-security contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the ruling: rahn and kafalah are ja'iz (permissible) in kharaj.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof: 'because it is a debt that is demandable and possible to collect'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the attribute 'demandable debt' triggers the validity of security contracts: contracts of pledge and suretyship require a debt that can be enforced.
4
Note the practical effect
Recognize that kharaj is treated like any other debt: non-payment can lead to imprisonment, and the creditor can pursue the debtor.
5
Recognize the rhetorical device
In the Arabic phrase, 'demandable' pairs with kafalah and 'possible to collect' with rahn (non-ordered laff wa nashr).
A linguistic benefit mentioned by the commentator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال والرهن والكفالة جائزان فى الخراج لانه دين مطالب به ممكن الاستيفاء فيمكن ترتيب موجب العقد عليه فيهما

ترجمہ خراج میں رہن اور کفالہ دونوں جائز ہیں۔ کیونکہ خراج ایک ایسا قرضہ ہے جس کا مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے ( اور ) اس کا وصول کرتا ممکن ہے پس رہن اور کفالہ دونوں میں عقد کے موجب کو اس پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے ۔

تشریح صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ خراج میں رہن اور کفالہ دونوں جائز ہیں۔ یعنی اگر کسی ذمی پر خراج واجب ہو اور اس کی طرف سے کوئی کفیل ہو گیا تو جائز ہے اور اگر اسے خراج کے عوض کچھ رہن دیا تو بھی جائز ہے۔ کفالہ تو اسلئے جائز ہے کہ کفالہ کہتے ہیں مطالبہ دین میں ایک ذمہ کو دوسرے ذمہ کے ساتھ ملانا اور خراج بھی ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے حتی کہ خراج ادانہ کرنے کی صورت میں ذمی کو محبوس کرایا جا سکتا ہے جیسا کہ دین ادانہ کرنے کی صورت میں مدیون اور قرضدار کو محبوس کرانا جائز ہے اور جس طرح دین ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں مدیون کا پیچھا اس طرح کیا جا سکتا ہے کہ دائن اس سے جدا نہ ہو اسی طرح خراج ادا نہ کرنے کی صورت میں ذمی کا پیچھا بھی کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ پس ثابت ہوا کہ خراج ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے اور ایسا دین جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جائے اس کا کفالہ جائز ہوتا ہے لہذ اخراج کا کفالہ بھی جائز ہوگا اور رہن اسلئے جائز ہے کہ رہن، دین وصول کرنے کا وثیقہ ہے۔ یعنی رہن کی صورت میں دین وصول ہونے کا اعتماد اور بھروسہ ہو جاتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح رہن سے چونکہ خراج وصول کرنا ممکن ہے اسلئے جس طرح دین کی صورت میں رہن جائز ہے اسی طرح خراج میں رہن رکھنا بھی جائز ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے اس بات کو مختصر ایوں فرمایا کہ خراج چونکہ ایسا دین ہے جس کا بندوں کی جانب سے مطالبہ کیا جاتا ہے اور رہن سے اس کا وصول کرنا بھی ممکن ہے اسلئے کفالہ اور رہن میں عقد کفالہ اور عقد رہن کے موجب کو خراج پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے اور جب کفالہ اور رہن میں ان کے موجب کو خراج پر مرتب کرنا ممکن ہے تو خراج میں کفالہ اور رہن دونوں جائز ہوں گے۔

فوائد عبارت میں چونکہ دین مطالب بہ کا تعلق کفالہ کے ساتھ ہے اور ممکن الاستیفاء کا تعلق رہن کے ساتھ ہے۔ اسلئے عبارت میں لف ونشر غیر مرتب ہوگا۔
He said: Rahn (pledge) and kafalah (suretyship) are permissible in kharaj (land tax) because it is a debt that is demandable and possible to collect, so it is possible to arrange the effect of the contract upon it in both. Translation: Rahn and kafalah are both permissible in kharaj. Because kharaj is a debt that is demanded and its collection is possible. Therefore, it is possible to arrange the effect of the contract upon it in both rahn and kafalah. Commentary: Sahib al-Quduri says that rahn and kafalah are both permissible in kharaj. That is, if a dhimmi owes kharaj and someone becomes his surety, it is valid; and if he gives something as pledge for the kharaj, it is also valid. Kafalah is valid because kafalah is joining one liability to another in demanding a debt, and kharaj is a debt that is demanded from the people. Even if kharaj is not paid, the dhimmi can be imprisoned, just as a debtor can be imprisoned for non-payment of a debt. And just as a debtor can be pursued so that the creditor does not separate from him, similarly for kharaj. Thus it is established that kharaj is a debt demanded from people, and kafalah for such a debt is valid. Hence kafalah for kharaj is valid. Rahn is valid because rahn is a security for collecting a debt. It instills confidence. Since collecting kharaj via rahn is possible, rahn for kharaj is permissible. The author of Hidayah summarized: since kharaj is a demandable debt and its collection via rahn is possible, the effect of the contracts of kafalah and rahn can be arranged upon it. Benefit: In the phrase, 'debt demandable' relates to kafalah, and 'possible to collect' relates to rahn, so there is non-ordered lafth wa nashr (a rhetorical device).
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam al-Quduri stating that both rahn (pledge) and kafalah (suretyship) are permissible in relation to kharaj (land tax). The proof is that kharaj is a debt that can be demanded (din mutalab bih) and is possible to collect (mumkin al-istifa'). Therefore, it is possible to arrange the effects of these contracts—namely, giving security and undertaking responsibility—upon kharaj. The commentator explains that kharaj is treated like any other debt: if a dhimmi fails to pay, he can be imprisoned or pursued, just as an ordinary debtor can. Hence, kafalah for kharaj is valid because it involves joining liability in a demandable debt. Similarly, rahn for kharaj is valid because rahn is a security for collection, and since kharaj can be collected, its security is valid. The passage also includes a linguistic note (fa'idah) about the rhetorical device of lafth wa nashr in the original Arabic phrase, where 'debt demandable' is paired with kafalah and 'possible to collect' with rahn, in non-ordered fashion.

Key Terms
الخراج (al-kharāj): Land tax imposed on non-Muslim subjects (dhimmīs) on agricultural land.
الرهن (al-rahn): Pledge or collateral given to secure a debt.
الكفالة (al-kafālah): Suretyship; joining one's liability to another for the purpose of demanding a debt or person.
دين مطالب به (dayn muṭālab bih): A debt that can be legally demanded and enforced.
ممكن الاستيفاء (mumkin al-istīfā'): Something that is possible to collect or receive in full.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is rahn permissible in kharaj according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because kharaj is a voluntary charity
B) Because kharaj is a demandable debt possible to collect
C) Because kharaj is like a gift
D) Because kharaj has no legal effect

Key Takeaway
Kharaj is a demandable debt; therefore, all valid debt-security contracts (rahn, kafalah) apply to it.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate

Multiple Sureties for the Same Person: Validity and Effect
Ruling on multiple sureties for the person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple sureties for the person and explain the reasoning based on the nature of demand and strengthening.

Core Idea
Multiple sureties for the same person are valid because demand is multiple and each surety independently strengthens the claim.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the validity of taking multiple sureties (kafalah bi al-nafs) for the same person. The passage explains why such multiple sureties are valid and do not conflict, using a rational argument based on the purpose of kafalah. Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying the law of suretyship in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taking a second surety for the same person after having already taken one. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The text states: 'فهما كفيلان' – so both are sureties.
2
Locate the dalil
The author uses a rational inference (ta'lil) based on the nature of kafalah: its effect is the obligation of demand (iltizam al-mutalabah), and demand can be multiple.
The Arabic: 'لان موجبه التزام المطالبة وهي متعددة'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The purpose of kafalah is strengthening (tawaththuq). A second surety increases strength, so there is no conflict between the two sureties.
The text: 'والمقصود التوثق وبالثانية يزداد التوثق فلايتنافيان'
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant dispute within the Hanafi school on this ruling. It is a standard position from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The cross-madhhab status is muttafaq alayh among Hanafis.
5
Apply the ruling
If one surety produces the person, that surety is discharged, but the other remains liable until the person is produced again. Each surety is independently bound.
Example from commentary: Shahid and Wasif both sureties; if Shahid produces Hamid, Shahid is freed but Wasif remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: ومن اخذ من رجل كفيلاً بنفسه ثم ذهب فاخذ منه كفيلاً آخر فهما كفيلان لان موجبه التزام المطالبة وهي متعددة والمقصود التوثق وبالثانية يزداد التوثق فلايتنافيان

ترجمہ اگر کسی نے ایک آدمی سے کفیل بالنفس لیا پھر جا کر دوسرا کفیل لیا تو یہ دونوں، دوکفیل ہوں گے اس لئے کہ عقد کفالہ کا موجب زام مطالبہ ہے اور مطالبہ متعدد ہے اور عقد کفالہ کا مقصود مضبوطی حاصل کرنا ہے اور دوسرے کفالہ سے مضبوطی بڑھ جائے گی الہذا دونوں کفالتوں میں منافات نہ ہو گی۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ آدمی کی طرف سے اگر متعدد کفیل ہو گئے تو صحیح ہے خواہ بیک وقت کفیل ہوئے ہوں خواہ یکے بعد دیگرے کفیل ہوئے ہوں مثلاً خالد قرض خواہ نے اپنے قرضدار حامد سے ایک کفیل بالنفس لیا یعنی شاہد قرضدار حامد کو حاضر کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا پھر خالد قرض خواہ نے حامد سے دوسرا کفیل بالنفس واصف کو لیا۔ یعنی واصف بھی حامد قرضدار کو حاضر کرنے کا کفیل ہو گیا تو یہ دونوں یعنی شاہد اور واصف دو فیل ہو جائیں گے اور ہر ایک ملکول بنفسہ (حامد) کو حاضر کرنے کا علیحدہ کفیل ہو گا حتی کہ ایک کفیل نے اگر مکفول بنفسہ کو حاضر کر دیا تو یہ بری ہو جائیگا مگر دوسرا کفیل بری نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ عقد کفالہ کا موجب اپنے اوپر مطالبہ کو لازم کرنا ہے اور مطالبہ متعدد ہے۔ چنانچہ فیل اور مکفول بنفسہ دونوں سے مطالبہ ہو سکتا ہے سنیل سے حاضر کرنے کا اور مکفول بنفسہ سے حاضر ہونے کا اور عقد کفالہ مشروع کرنے سے مقصود مضبوطی کا حاصل ہونا ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ دوسرے کفالہ سے مضبوطی بڑھے گی نہ کہ گھٹے گی ۔ پس جب دوسرا کفالہ مضبوطی میں اضافہ کرتا ہے تو ان دونوں کفالتوں میں منافات نہ ہوگی۔ اور جب دونوں کفالتوں میں منافات نہیں ہے تو دونوں کفالتیں جائز ہوں گی ۔
He said: And whoever takes a surety for the person from a man, then goes and takes another surety for the person from him, then they are both sureties because its effect is the obligation of demand, and demand is multiple, and the purpose is strengthening, and by the second strengthening increases, so they do not conflict. Translation: If someone took a surety for the person from a man, then went and took another surety for the person, then both are two sureties, because the effect of the contract of kafalah is the obligation of demand, and demand is multiple, and the purpose of kafalah is to obtain strength, and with the second kafalah strength increases, so there is no contradiction between the two. Commentary: The issue is that if multiple sureties become surety for a person, it is valid whether simultaneously or successively. Example: Khalid, the creditor, took a surety for the person from his debtor Hamid, i.e., Shahid became surety for producing Hamid. Then Khalid took another surety, Wasif. Then both Shahid and Wasif become two sureties, each separate. If one surety produces the person, he is discharged but the other is not. The reasoning is that the effect of kafalah is to make demand obligatory on oneself, and demand is multiple. So both the surety and the person can be demanded. The purpose is strength, and the second increases strength, so no contradiction, thus both valid.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling about multiple sureties for the person (kafalah bi al-nafs). If someone takes one surety for a person and later takes another surety for the same person, both are sureties and their obligations do not conflict. The reason given is that the effect of kafalah is to obligate the demand (iltizam al-mutalabah) for the person's presence. Since demand can be made against multiple parties—both the original person and multiple sureties—having multiple sureties does not contradict the purpose. In fact, the purpose of kafalah is to strengthen the claim (tawaththuq), and the second surety increases that strength. Therefore, both sureties are valid, and each is separately responsible. If one surety produces the person, that surety is discharged, but the other remains bound until the person is produced again. This shows that the obligation is not shared but each is independently liable for the demand of the person.

Key Terms
كفيل بالنفس (kafil bi al-nafs): A surety responsible for producing the person (the mukful bi al-nafs) when demanded.
التزام المطالبة (iltizām al-muṭālabah): The undertaking of the obligation to respond to the demand for the person or debt.
التوثق (al-tawaththuq): Strengthening or securing the claim; the purpose of kafalah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if one surety for a person produces the person?
A) Both sureties are discharged
B) The producing surety is discharged, the other remains
C) The other surety is also discharged automatically
D) The person must be produced again by both

Key Takeaway
Multiple sureties for the person are valid and each is independently liable; producing the person discharges only the producing surety.
